The Implementation Measures and Plans for the Protection of Fisheries Are Approved

The Executive Yuan held its 24th meeting on the 2nd. The attendees were Song Ziwen, Ma Fuxiang, Liu Ruiheng, Wang Boqun, Kong Xiangxi, Wang Zhengting, Lie Li Shuhua, Chen Yi, Chen Shaokuan, and Lian Shenghai, with Secretary-General Lü Bichou presiding. Song Ziwen reported on 23 matters and discussed 20 matters. The discussed matters announced are as follows: (1) The Secretariat forwarded the joint letter from the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education on the matter of establishing a National History Museum, which was submitted for review and discussion. After discussion, it was generally agreed that the compilation of national history should be recorded permanently and shown to future generations, and it is necessary to establish an agency to select personnel to handle it. Whether the name should be National History Museum or National History Compilation Committee, and whether it should be under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Interior after its official establishment or under the jurisdiction of a certain agency as originally proposed, are all subject to the decision of the Executive Yuan. However, during the preparatory period, whether it can be jointly handled by the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education, or whether a special commissioner should be appointed to oversee it, are all submitted for review and instructions. It was resolved that the Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Education should temporarily prepare for it. (2) The Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of the Navy, and the Ministry of Industry jointly presented the implementation measures for the protection of fisheries for review and approval. In addition, the Ministry of Industry presented the entire plan for the protection of fisheries for review and approval. It was resolved to follow the plan. (3) The Ministry of Interior and the Ministry of Industry jointly presented the draft regulations on fisheries police, which were jointly drafted by the former Ministry of Agriculture and Mines and the Ministry of Interior, and have now been revised. The revised draft regulations are presented for review, approval, and implementation. It was resolved to follow the plan. (4) It was resolved to reorganize the Agricultural, Mining, and Commerce Bureaus of Shanxi Province into an Industry Bureau, and to request the reappointment of Chang Bingyi as the director of the Industry Bureau. (5) It was resolved to reorganize the Agricultural and Mining Bureau of Guizhou Province into an Industry Bureau, and to request the reappointment of Du Yunshu as the director of the Industry Bureau. (6) It was resolved to approve the resignation of Hua Jueming, the Secretary-General of the Hubei Provincial Government, and to request the appointment of Peng Jieshi concurrently as the Secretary-General of the Hubei Provincial Government. (7) It was resolved to request the transfer of Mo Linhang to be the colonel of the Military Supply School of the Military Supply Department of the Ministry of Military Affairs and Wu Jimin to be the colonel director of training.

Guangzhou Consecutive Bombing Cases 37

Destroyed the Provincial Government's Right Side Perimeter Wall

Guangzhou Correspondence: Following the explosion at the gunpowder depot, the "Central Pillar," in Guangdong Province, two bomb cases occurred in the city on the evenings of May 25th and 26th. On the 25th, at 9:00 PM and 9:50 PM, respectively, there were two loud explosions originating near Central Park. Less than ten minutes separated the blasts. As a result, residents on Desheng, Hui'ai, Yuehua, Guangda, Guangwei, and other roads near Central Park closed their doors early, and shops immediately ceased night market activities. After investigation, it was discovered that the bombs were thrown under the perimeter wall on the right side of the Provincial Government on Jixiang Road. The opposite side of the wall is Hou Lou Fang (street name), which is connected in all directions. Therefore, after the explosion, the bomber escaped from an unknown location and could not be apprehended. Yuan, the director of the Desheng Police Sub-bureau, upon hearing the news, immediately led a large contingent of armed police to investigate. Simultaneously, the Public Security Bureau and the Military Police Command also dispatched teams to search for suspects in the vicinity. The military police guarding the Provincial Government also dispatched sentries that evening to prevent any accidents. That evening, all members of the Provincial and Municipal Party Headquarters were holding a public banquet for military and political figures at the Provincial Party Headquarters in Dadongmen. Chen Jitang, upon hearing the news, immediately instructed Military Police Commander Lin Shiqing and Public Security Bureau Chief Chen Qingyun to dispatch teams to investigate strictly. However, before the cause of this case could be determined, two more explosions occurred on Changdi Jiulixiang Heng Street at approximately 9:00 PM the following evening (May 26th). The left side of the street entrance is the former headquarters of the Sixty-third Division, and the right side is the National Garden Hall. The destructive power of the bombs there was less than that of the bombs on the 25th. The bombs on the 25th destroyed a section of the perimeter wall on the right side of the Provincial Government and penetrated the ground to a depth of about three feet. The bombs on Jiulixiang Heng Street did not destroy anything. (May 27th)

Lu Dipin Returns to Jiangxi from Nanjing 38

Lu States That the Jiangxi Bandits Have Not Been Eliminated, and the Troops Will Not Be Transferred Elsewhere. There Are Methods for Post-War Rehabilitation and Financial Relief in the Bandit Areas.

Nanchang Correspondence: Lu Dipin, Chairman of the Jiangxi Provincial Government and concurrently Commander-in-Chief of the Ninth Route Army, went to Nanjing last month to attend the National Assembly and to negotiate with the central government regarding post-war rehabilitation, financial relief in the bandit areas, and future steps in suppressing the bandits. Lu believed that all matters had been settled, and since the province was in the midst of bandit suppression, it was necessary to return to the province to preside over military and political affairs. He took a boat back to Jiangxi from Nanjing on the 28th, and arrived in the province at 12:00 PM on the 30th via the Nanchang-Xun Railway special train from Xunyang. At that time, Wang , representative of Minister He, the two Department Heads, Cao, the Deputy Adjutant of the Ninth Route Army Headquarters, and representatives of various organization leaders and groups were all at Niuhang Station to welcome him. From Niuhang Station to the Provincial Government, along the Jiangzhongshan and Deshenglu areas, the Eighteenth Division, the Fifty-second Division, the Second Provincial Security Regiment, and the Provincial Security Team increased patrols for protection. After Lu crossed the river with the welcoming party, he took a car to the military camp to meet with Minister He, reported on the situation in Nanjing, and discussed the methods determined by the central government for future bandit suppression. After about an hour of discussion, he left and went to the Provincial Government, where all the members of the Provincial Government were waiting. Lu spoke to the government members, saying that he had been in charge of Jiangxi's administration for two years without any success, and the disturbances caused by the communists made it impossible to carry out any construction. Therefore, he had requested to resign from the central government during this trip to Nanjing. The central government and Chairman Chiang Kai-shek encouraged him to work together during these difficult times and to fulfill his responsibilities as a party member. He had no choice but to return to Jiangxi to preside over the administration. The central government paid great attention to the bandit problem in the province and decided to devote all its efforts to eliminate Zhu Mao and other communist bandits in the shortest possible time according to the established plan. Because the communist bandits not only endanger the party and the country, but also endanger world security. Before all the bandit factions are eliminated, the troops will only be increased and never reduced or transferred elsewhere. Therefore, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek has consistently stated that the suppression of bandits in the province will not be affected by the Guangdong affair. After the Chen Jiang telegram was issued in Guangdong, the central government consistently advocated leniency in the hope that they would repent. If Chen Jitang and others insisted on reopening the war, causing suffering to the people and creating opportunities for the communist bandits, then the central government would quickly eliminate them. In addition, the central government approved the issuance of post-war public bonds, subsidies for administrative expenses and disaster relief, and exemptions from bearing the costs of grain and allowances for the suppression of bandits, all of which had satisfactory results. The newly appointed Director of Finance, Yang Mianzhong (formerly Secretary-General of the Provincial Government), has recently been in Nanjing negotiating with Finance Minister Song Ziwen regarding the province's relief finance and all post-war matters, and will return to the province to take office in the next day or two. After leaving the Provincial Government, Lu went to the Twenty-eighth Division's garrison to comfort Commander Gong and inquire about the battles of Donggu and Futian and the recent situation on the front lines. Gong has already gone to Nanjing from the province on the 31st to report to Chiang Kai-shek on the progress of bandit suppression in Jiangxi and to request instructions. (June 1st)

Jiaoji Railway Coal Merchants Resume Transportation 40

Still Implemented According to the Ministry's Approved Freight Rate

Temporarily Give Coal Merchants a 20% Rebate

Jinan Correspondence: The coal merchants' strike in Boshan and Zichuan has lasted for ten days. Yesterday, more than twenty small coal merchants at the mines, unable to withstand the losses of the strike, planned to load cars and resume operations, but were dispersed by crowds from the Coal Industry Association's Children's School in the strike group. Operations are still suspended today. Ge Guangting, the Chairman of the Jiaoji Railway Committee, went to Nanjing to request instructions on the issues of increased freight rates and Jiaoji Railway interest. He arrived in Jinan from Nanjing at 7:30 PM today (21st). When a reporter interviewed him on the train, he said that since the implementation of the Jiaoji Railway's increased freight rates, there has been a coal merchants' strike. The provincial government suspects that the railway is acting too aggressively. In fact, this case was handled in accordance with the ministry's orders. How dare the railway increase prices without authorization? Currently, the Ministry of Railways' attitude is to blame the former Director of Business for the responsibility of increasing prices. It seems that freight rates can be slightly reduced. To what extent they can be reduced is not yet known, but the ministry's orders are difficult to retract, which is quite hesitant. The Jiaoji Railway's debt to Japanese interest cannot be paid due to the sharp rise in gold prices. This is also one of the tasks of my trip to Nanjing. Because if we pay such a huge amount of interest, the railway's expenses will not be sustainable. Therefore, we asked the Ministry of Railways for additional subsidies. Although the ministry agreed to our request, whether it can subsidize us under the current central government situation is still a question. According to Tan Shukui, the Director of the Jiaoji Railway's Car Affairs Office, since the coal merchants' strike, the provincial government has been concerned about its impact on local order and people's livelihood. It has consulted with the railway authorities several times to find a solution. Because the price increase was approved by the National Government Council and the Ministry of Railways' orders, the railway did not dare to act without authorization. Chairman Han Fuju and Wang Fangting, the Director of the Department of Agriculture and Mines, both intended to first order the coal merchants to resume operations and then refund the amount after the price reduction was approved, but the coal merchants refused, so there was no solution. Chairman Han and Director Wang are now advocating stabilizing coal prices, stipulating the price of coal at the mines and the freight rate fairly, and prohibiting market prices from being raised and hoarding. This matter will be resolved simultaneously with the freight rate issue.

Furthermore, this evening (31st) at 7:00 PM, we received a continuation call from Ge Guangting, the Chairman of the Jiaoji Railway Committee, stating that the coal mines will resume operations from June 1st. The method is to temporarily give the coal mines a 20% rebate on the current freight rate, and the railway bureau will actually receive 80% in cash. In this way, the ministry's orders can be maintained, and the coal mines' demands have also been achieved. (May 31st)

The Business Community in Beiping and Tianjin Strongly Opposes the Production and Sales Tax 41

Wang Shuchang Goes to Beiping to Request Instructions from Zhang Xueliang

The Beiping Chamber of Commerce Prepares for a City-Wide Strike

The Production and Sales Tax Bureau Actually Implements Confiscation of Goods

The Special Commissioner's Office of Finance Declares That It Is Not Extortion

The Tianjin business community, due to its opposition to the production and sales tax, previously sent Wang Wendian to Beiping to meet with Zhang Xueliang to present everything. Wang returned to Tianjin on the evening of the 28th because he did not get to see Zhang. On the morning of the 29th, he accompanied Zhang Pintai, the Chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, to meet with Wang Shuchang, the Chairman of the Hebei Provincial Government, who personally received them. Zhang Pintai stated that after the abolition of likin, the production and sales tax was added, which is more harmful than likin, and other provinces do not have this tax. The National Government also has no orders to implement this tax, nor has it been approved by the provincial government. If it is not abolished, merchants can only suspend business. Wang agreed to go to Beiping that night to report to Zhang Xueliang and request instructions. In the afternoon, Zhang Pintai convened a meeting of representatives from various trades in the Chamber of Commerce to report on the results of the meeting with Wang. After discussion, it was decided to send Wang Wendian to Nanjing and Zhang Pintai to Beiping to appeal separately. If they are not accepted, they will implement the second step of a city-wide strike movement in conjunction with various counties and cities. It was also decided that on the morning of the 30th, representatives would go to the Municipal Readjustment Committee to meet with Liu Butong to ask him to help find a solution, and also submit a report to the Department of Industry to appeal. However, the tax bureau, due to the merchants' refusal to pay taxes, ordered the confiscation of goods in order to force the merchants to yield. The confiscation of goods has been relentless for days. On the 29th, Yongjufeng, a shop in Xincheng Chaha Ji, entrusted Wang, a boatman, to purchase nine small coarse porcelain jars worth nine yuan. They were confiscated by tax bureau patrol officers at Ganqiao in Beiyingmen. After negotiations, a fine of two yuan was paid before they were released.

The opposition to the production and sales tax in the Beiping business community is intensifying. The tax bureau has also been ordered to confiscate goods and levy taxes, which has further provoked opposition from the business community, and has requested the Special Commissioner's Office of Finance to return the confiscated goods, otherwise they will implement a strike. The office had no choice but to approve a temporary suspension of collection from May 30th and return the confiscated goods. However, as of 3-4 PM on the 30th, goods were still not allowed to enter the city through Fuchengmen, Andingmen, and Guang'anmen. It was reported that the hides detained in Changxindian had not yet been returned. The Fengtai Transportation Industry Association reported that 60-70 trucks of goods detained by the association had not been returned, or may be returned today (31st). The representatives of various trades in Beiping, who had previously petitioned, gathered again at 9:00 AM on the morning of the 30th, with 500 people going to the Chamber of Commerce for a temporary representative meeting. Chairman Leng Jiaji and various representatives spoke at length, their expressions were very excited, saying that Vice Commander Zhang Xueliang has always protected the merchants, and this production and sales tax is definitely not Vice Commander Zhang's own intention, but purely the initiative of a certain person. We should die and oppose it, and some even proposed building a bronze statue for a certain person. Finally, it was decided that if the production and sales tax cannot be cancelled before June 2nd, all the shops in the city will strike on the 3rd. In addition, Gao Ziliang, Yang Jixian, Sun Kuifu, and Zou Quansun were appointed to go to Zhang's residence in Xinjian Hutong at 4:00 PM on the afternoon of the 30th to petition and visit Jing Youyan, the Special Commissioner of Finance, and ask him to quickly return the confiscated goods. The meeting adjourned around 12:00 PM. Gao and others first went to the Special Commissioner's Office of Finance at 4:00 PM. Jing stated that the confiscated goods would be returned immediately. The representatives then went to Xinjian Hutong, but because Zhang was still ill, Zhu Guangmu received them on his behalf. The representatives expressed their eagerness to meet with the Vice Commander. Zhu stated that Zhang was not fully recovered and asked the representatives to visit Ji Yiqiao, the Chief of Staff of the headquarters, first. The representatives then left. According to a letter from the Joss Stick and Traditional Medicine Guild to the Chamber of Commerce, Wanxing Incense Factory transported elm noodles from Pingxi by camel, and when they arrived at Changxindian, the tax bureau ordered them to pay a tax of 17 yuan per thousand catties. According to the old regulations, the tax was 8 jiao per thousand catties, but now it has exceeded 20 times, which is really unbearable. In addition, the Xingtai Chamber of Commerce sent representatives Liu Xiangqing, Yang Yunlong, and Jia Zhao to Beiping yesterday to cancel the production and sales tax. According to their remarks, the tax bureau ordered a person carrying two dou of soybeans into the city to pay a tax of 1 yuan and 2 jiao. The severity of this tax can be seen.

The Hebei Finance Special Commissioner's Office issued a statement regarding the telegram sent to Vice Commander Zhang by the Beiping Municipal Chamber of Commerce on the 29th: After reading the reports published in Beiping and Tianjin newspapers on the 29th of this month, the various statements made by Leng Jiaji, the Chairman of the Beiping Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and others in the telegram to Vice Commander Zhang regarding the production and sales tax implemented by the office under orders are deeply regrettable. The telegram stated that the production and sales tax exceeds the Chongguan tax by more than ten or twenty times. I don't know that the Chongguan tax is a unique and harsh tax in Beiping. The merits and demerits of the production and sales tax have been explained in detail by the office in Beiping and Tianjin newspapers on the same day. How can they be compared? Even the tax rates cited in the telegram contain many inaccuracies. For example, for lambskin, the production and sales tax schedule in Appendix 1 states that raw and cooked lambskins from Mongolia, Shunde, and other places are taxed at 8 fen or 1 jiao 4 li per skin, which is 8 yuan or 10 yuan and 4 jiao per hundred skins. Only Tibetan Daying lambskins, which are luxury goods, have a higher tax rate. How can it be collectively referred to as 21 yuan per hundred skins? Also, for cat skin, the same table states that the tax is 1 fen 6 li 5 per flowered cat skin and 3 fen 3 li per black and white dyed cat skin. How can it be falsely claimed that the tax is 4 fen per skin? Comparing it with the Chongguan tax, although the tax rate for luxury goods is occasionally increased, there has never been an increase of more than ten or twenty times. The fish tax, although it existed in the Chongguan tax, has been completely exempted from the production and sales tax. It is even more unknown what the basis is for the telegram's claim that the tax is now 4 yuan and 8 jiao. This is very surprising. From these various points, it can be seen that the merchants have not researched the production and sales tax rates at all, and the Beiping Municipal Chamber of Commerce has not carefully examined them before forwarding them in accordance with the regulations. It is not necessary to delve into the fact that the office is acting under orders, but such unfounded rumors and sensationalism not only affect tax revenue, but also fear that they will lead to misunderstandings that harm public order, thereby delaying important political affairs. Who will bear the blame? In short, the country cannot stop government affairs for a day, and it cannot stop tax collection for a day. Extortion is certainly wrong, but can resistance be said to be right? Under the current financial situation in Hebei, even if the production and sales tax is cancelled as the merchants wish, what method will be used to compensate for the insufficient military and administrative expenses after the abolition of likin? Although the positions of government officials and the people are different, understanding should be consistent. Mutual tolerance and assistance are necessary to achieve success. As for the claim that willow coffins are taxed at 7% and yellow earth handcarts are taxed at 1 jiao 5 fen, if this is true, it is the illegal extortion of the collecting officials. It is hoped that the victimized merchants will report the evidence to the office by name. Once verified, they will be punished according to the law and will not be tolerated as a warning to other lawbreakers. It is also hoped that the chambers of commerce in various places will report any illegal behavior of the collecting officials of each bureau at any time, openly or secretly, without any concealment, to assist the office in handling this matter. The original intention of the office in implementing this production and sales tax is sincerely hoped that the business community will understand. (May 31st)

Japanese People Actively Progressing in Manchuria and Mongolia 42

Japanese Residents in Northeast China Organize an Autonomous League

Merchants and Warlords Collude to Promote Independence

All Want to Oppose Railway Negotiations and Concessions

Changchun Correspondence: Japanese residents along the South Manchuria Railway (SMR), led by Mr. Kimura, have been meeting in Liaoning for many days to discuss railway negotiations, but there has been no progress. They are deeply concerned about the threat to their imperial rights, so they specifically initiated a Northeast Japanese Residents' Representative Conference. The conference was held in Shenyang on the 22nd of this month, and 52 representatives from various regions attended. They deliberated for several days until the 24th, when they decided to organize the All Manchuria Japanese Autonomous League to solicit members and formulate rules. Japanese residents in various regions sent telegrams to join the league upon hearing the news, and there are already more than 400 members. The ten articles of the league's constitution are as follows: Article 1: This league is named the All Manchuria Japanese Autonomous League. This league is located in Fengtian, and other branches are located in various places. Article 2: The purpose of this league is to maintain imperial rights and develop the Japanese nation. Article 3: Japanese residents in Manchuria who agree with the purpose of the preceding article shall organize this league. Article 4: In order to achieve the purpose of Article 2, all necessary tasks must be carried out. Article 5: This league shall have the following officers with a term of one year. Article 6: There shall be one director, several standing directors, and several directors. Each region shall have one branch director. Article 7: Directors shall be elected by the general meeting, standing directors shall be elected by the officers' meeting, and branch directors shall be elected by the branches. Article 8: The officers' meeting shall be composed of the director, directors, standing directors, and branch directors. Article 9: The tasks of this league shall be decided by the officers' meeting and implemented by the directors. Article 10: The expenses shall be donated by league members and other parties. Mr. Ueda, the representative of the Japanese residents in Shenyang, was elected as the director. The passed resolutions were: (1) If the Chinese loan railway does not pay the principal and interest, it shall be forcibly executed or its railway shall be taken over. (2) Remove the intersections with the Beining Railway. (3) Suspend the joint operation of the Datong Railway. (The above resolutions were sent to Mr. Kimura to be proposed at the current railway conference.) (4) Oppose China's abolition of consular jurisdiction. (5) If Mr. Kimura's negotiations fail, the government must take decisive measures regarding Manchuria's railway rights. (6) Oppose Shidehara's diplomatic policy against public opinion. (7) Oppose China's collection of five import taxes on Japanese goods, such as cotton yarn, flour, matches, and tobacco. (The above was submitted to the government by Mr. Yoshida, the Director of the Fanyang Chamber of Commerce in Nanjing, upon his arrival in Tokyo.) It was also decided to notify the results of this conference to Japanese residents in various regions to pay attention and solicit Japanese residents in various regions to join the league to expand its influence. It can also be seen that the Japanese residents' ambitions are rampant. Our countrymen should not ignore it.

According to the World News Agency in Tokyo, recently the voices of our country abolishing consular jurisdiction have been rising, and the National Assembly has announced the denial of all unequal treaties to show our country's greatest determination to abolish treaties. Our closest neighbor, Japan, is paying close attention to this. Those who are slightly aware of the times are all discussing goodwill, while the military and commercial warlords in China are colluding with each other to actively oppose diplomatic concessions to China. The All Japan Chamber of Commerce has even resolved to petition the government on three items: opposing the abolition of consular jurisdiction and supporting Manchuria and Mongolia's rights and interests. The most powerful force in opposing diplomatic concessions to China is the South Manchuria Railway Company (SMR). It is currently conducting the Northeast Railway negotiations. The intentions of Sima Zhao are known to everyone. On the other hand, it is also trying to plan the so-called Manchuria and Mongolia development plan centered on the SMR. Its meaning is that if the Northeast authorities do not recognize the right to lay five major railways, then it plans to focus on operating the SMR to control Manchuria and Mongolia's rights and interests. Recently, the SMR has been demanding the independence of the SMR's operations from the government authorities in Tokyo. The so-called independence does not mean that it is not subject to government control, but that it does not change with the change of government. As for economic policies, it is also exempt from being controlled by government authorities. In the future, it plans to establish a supreme council to recruit former SMR presidents and powerful figures from the private sector to give the agency the power to decide on the president and operating policies. Regarding this proposal, SMR executives such as Muno Shigekuro, Yamakawa Duofu, and Nakagawa Masa left one after another to return to Japan to contact the authorities.

The Department of Construction previously issued a notice to each county government to establish farmers' banks. The Department of Construction promotes agriculture and is now planning to pilot public rice seedling fields to benefit farmers. Wuxi 46

A Boy Bitten to Death by a Loach: Zhao Genfu, a cook by trade and resident of Houqi Street outside the North Gate, had an eight-year-old son named A'er. Recently, a neighbor, Mr. Jia, dug up a gray pond in the field and caught three loaches, keeping them in a water tank. The other day, the child went to the neighbor's house and leaned against the tank to play with water. Unexpectedly, the loaches were disturbed and began to swim wildly. One of the loaches, fiery yellow in color, suddenly leaped out of the tank and bit A'er fiercely on the back of his foot. Immediately, fresh blood flowed, and he fell to the ground in pain. His father, Genfu, noticed and rushed him to Dr. Zhou Shinong Tan Shumo's clinic for treatment. However, the poison was too deep, and treatment was ineffective. He died from the poison yesterday, a truly tragic event. It is rumored that what Mr. Jia caught was not a loach but a red-banded snake. Therefore, A'er was bitten to death. Zhao Genfu plans to negotiate with Mr. Jia.

A Strange Homicide in Lixiang: Li Zhilin, a farmer from Lixiang, the 142nd Tu of the 16th District of this county, is 19 years old. In February of this year, he married Ms. Han, the daughter of Gong Gentang, through a matchmaker. After she entered his home, their relationship was not harmonious. On the night of April 6th of the lunar calendar, Ms. Gong stole a Gengtie (marriage certificate), eight paper sheets of field deeds, and gold and silver jewelry and fled. Her husband, upon learning this, went to his father-in-law's house to search for her but could not find her. On the 10th, her brother, A'quan, found her and brought her back, but she only returned six sheets of field deeds. Unexpectedly, on the night of the 15th, Ms. Gong suddenly fled again. Her husband searched everywhere but could not find her. The next afternoon, Ms. Gong's body was suddenly discovered in the Banyebang River. Zhilin, upon learning this, was about to report it to the county court for an autopsy. However, his father-in-law, Gong Gentang, had also learned of his daughter's tragic death and led his relatives to retrieve the body and carry it to his son-in-law's house, damaging the house in the process. Yesterday (the 2nd), Li Zhilin reported the incident to the county court. At the same time, the Tu Zheng (local head) of the area, Kuang Bo'an, also reported to the court. However, local gossip suggests that Ms. Gong was murdered by her husband. After receiving the report, the county court had Prosecutor Zhu open a court session for interrogation and ordered an official to go to the countryside today for an autopsy to gather evidence.

Robbery and Murder by Bandits: Zhang Gengquan, a farmer in the Beizhou Lane area of the 495th Tu of the Daidian Township in the 7th District of this county, had his new house robbed in November of last year, resulting in a loss of over 200 yuan. Unexpectedly, yesterday (the 1st) at around 1:00 AM, more than ten bandits, speaking in a strong northern accent, with white cloths wrapped around their heads and carrying flashlights, sharp knives, wooden sticks, and other weapons, opened the gate of the old house. Five bandits entered to search for valuables, while the rest stood guard outside, forcing Gengquan to reveal the location of his hidden silver. Gengquan, claiming that there was no silver in the house, angered the bandits, who hung him from the beam inside the gate and beat him severely. Because Gengquan had no silver to reveal, the bandits became even more enraged and stabbed him in the Tianmen acupoint on his head with a sharp knife, causing him to bleed profusely. Because they found nothing, the bandits took two dou of white rice, thirty ducks, and some scattered clothing and fled. Zhang's sons, A'da and A'lin, learned of the incident at the new house and rushed to save their father from the beam, but he had already died from his injuries. The next day, the Tu Zheng of the area, Lu Yongru, came to the city to report to the county court. Prosecutor Zhu opened a court session for interrogation and decided to go to the countryside today for an autopsy to gather evidence for the arrest and prosecution of the criminals.

Boy Injured by Exploding Ammunition: Huang Rongrui, a villager in Qianqiao Town (Kaiyuanxiang) in the 4th District, is a farmer by trade and raises several oxen for plowing, so he hired a shepherd boy named Lu Hongsheng, who is 14 years old. The other day, early in the morning, Lu Hongsheng returned home after herding the cattle and went to the field to work with a hoe. Unexpectedly, there was a piece of ammunition left over from the Jiazi War (Sino-Japanese War) in the field. It was struck by the iron hoe, and with a loud bang, it exploded, sending shrapnel flying. The shrapnel pierced Hongsheng's left knee, causing blood and flesh to splatter. He collapsed in extreme pain and lost consciousness. Passersby noticed and reported it to his master, who sent the injured boy to Tongren Hospital in the city for treatment. According to the hospital doctor, the knee bone has been shattered, and he may become disabled.

Construction Industry Requests Exemption from Business Tax: The Wuxi Construction Industry Association, with the impending imposition of business tax and the letter from the County Chamber of Commerce urging them to quickly send responsible representatives to negotiate the tax amount with the Business Tax Bureau, convened a meeting of all members to discuss. They all agreed that the construction industry is a labor-intensive industry and should not be subject to business tax. The bricks, tiles, and wood used in building houses are all subject to business tax paid by the respective merchants. Contractors only purchase on behalf of employers and have no profit to gain. Their actual income is only a small profit from the contracting work. If the total amount of wages is used as the basis for the business tax, it will not only cause an uproar among the workers, but it will also violate the government's intention to protect workers. If business tax is levied on the purchase of materials, it would be redundant and truly oppressive. Yesterday, a letter was sent to the Chamber of Commerce requesting that it be forwarded to the Business Tax Bureau and submitted to the Provincial Government requesting exemption from business tax.

Jiangyin 47

Order from the Provincial Government: Magistrate of Jingjiang County to Postpone Relinquishing Office: The former magistrate Li Leng of Jingjiang County, after receiving an order from the Civil Affairs Department to be transferred to the position of Magistrate of Jingjiang County, handed over his duties on the 23rd and then went to Jiading and Wujin. He was originally scheduled to go to Jingjiang yesterday (the 1st) to take up his new post. However, Magistrate Wang Jiwu of Jingjiang County received a telegram from the Civil Affairs Department, No. 637, on the 30th of last month, ordering the magistrate to postpone relinquishing office and await further instructions. Magistrate Wang immediately complied with the order. It is rumored that the reason is that Li Leng has been accused of opium bribery, and the local court has scheduled a hearing for the 15th, requiring the summons of the relevant individuals Huang Bingying, Qian Zuopeng, Hu A'yu, Chen Xiangbao, Wu Shanshi, and the editor of the Cheng Qing Party newspaper, Jiang Sheng, Wang Sengru, for interrogation. In addition, Huang Bingying's case of alleged defamation has been approved for transfer of jurisdiction to the Higher Court, with the first instance to be tried by the Wuxi court.

Investigating Officer Wu Goes to Jingjiang to Investigate: Chen Xingmin of Jingjiang has filed a complaint with the Higher Court against Magistrate Wang for embezzling 68,000 yuan in fines from opium cases, of which 30%, or 20,400 yuan, was allocated to the anti-opium bureau and prison expenses. The Higher Court has ordered Wu Shaoyu, a trial officer from Jiangyin, to go to Jingjiang to investigate. Wu arrived in Jingjiang to investigate and returned to Cheng yesterday evening.

Nantong 48

Director of Wounded Soldiers Factory Explains Misunderstanding: The 11th Division stationed in Hankou has sent Zhuang Mingyuan to be the director of the Nantong Wounded Soldiers Factory. The first batch of 84 wounded soldiers has arrived. All sectors of the local community, having previously suffered from the pain caused by wounded soldiers, unanimously oppose the factory. At 8:00 PM on the 31st, Director Zhuang hosted a reception for all sectors of the community at the Nantong Club to explain the misunderstanding. He also stated that he would accommodate local public opinion and submit a report to the General Headquarters and Commander Luo. Currently, officers and soldiers are waiting in Nantong for orders. Representatives from all sectors of the community gave speeches, stating that the local area's fear of the term "wounded soldiers" has caused a misunderstanding and that there are no other intentions.

Rugao 49

Chief of Police Enters Home at Night, Killing Housewife: Zhou Deshu of Wuliu, west of Meinihu, Lugang District, Rugao, owns more than 200 mu of fertile land and can be considered wealthy in the area. His wife, Zhang, is 34 years old. At approximately 9:00 PM on the 28th, Xu, the patrol captain of the 15th branch of the district's Public Security Bureau, along with five patrolmen including Li Hanzhang, dressed in military uniforms and plain clothes, carrying weapons, arrived at Zhou's house. Zhou's family was not yet asleep and heard someone knocking on the door. Zhou's wife, Zhang, fearing they were bandits, refused to open the door and told her husband to guard the windows. Seeing that no one was opening the door, the police chief and others opened fire on the door. One bullet flew through and struck Zhang in the head, shattering her skull and killing her instantly. The police chief and others then used wooden sticks to break down the door and searched the house with flashlights. Seeing Zhang lying in a pool of blood, they realized they had caused trouble and fled. Afterwards, Zhou went to the branch bureau to report the incident. Chief Shu immediately placed the five perpetrators under surveillance and reported the matter to the county bureau. After receiving the report, Chief Wang sent Inspector Qiu Bogao to the area to investigate and ordered the five perpetrators to be taken to the city for interrogation.

Gaoyou 50

Missing Boy Suddenly Found in Field: Wu Qi, a farmer from Xiajiaji Village in the 10th District of this county, had several bandits break into his house on the night of April 19th. After robbing them, they kidnapped his young son. He immediately reported the incident to the county government for strict investigation, but there had been no news for several weeks. Unexpectedly, Wu suddenly heard a child crying in the field the other night. He opened the door to look and saw that it was his son. He picked him up and was overjoyed. He has already come to the city to report to the county government for record.

Bandits Injure People in Yongzhuang Township: Xie Yu, a farmer in Yongzhuang Township in the 10th District of this county, had four bandits break into his house the other night, each carrying firearms. They broke down the door and searched the house extensively. Because they did not find much, the bandits beat Xie Yu and his wife severely with wooden sticks, causing serious injuries. It is feared that their lives are in danger.

Liuhe 51

Teacher Wage Arrears Still Difficult to Resolve: Education throughout Liuhe County has been at a standstill for over a week. The education authorities are helpless. Yesterday (31st) at 2:00 PM, teachers and staff met at the county girls' school to discuss ways to demand their salaries. They elected Jiang Chonglin, Dai Jiaji, and others as representatives to request the county government to release the arrears and to personally report the facts of the salary arrears to the provincial government.

Pinghu 52

Walking in the Dark, Fell into River and Drowned: Tao Ousheng of Xincang Town was walking home from town the other night. It was dark and the road was muddy. He lost his footing while crossing the East Ma Bridge and fell into the river. The area was cold and sparsely populated, and no one could rescue him. He drowned immediately.

Fishermen Encountered Danger While Fishing and Drowned: Yesterday, fishermen A'yao and others were fishing with nets in the outer sea of Zhapu when the sampan capsized due to rough tides. The fishermen on the beach could not help. A'yao and others drifted with the water until they reached the shallow waters of Zhengjiatai, where they were rescued by local residents, but they were already unconscious. Emergency resuscitation methods were used to revive them.

Xiaoshan 53

Courier for Riot Suppression Bureau Flees with Funds: Li Guisheng, a courier for the Xiaoshan County Riot Suppression Bureau, was introduced by Chen Fulin, a worker at the county government. On the 28th, he was sent to Heshangdian to deliver official documents. The county government ordered him to send 50 yuan in local self-government donations to the No. 3 district public office for verification. Unexpectedly, the courier fled with the funds. The county government was initially unaware of this until yesterday, when it received a letter from the courier stating that the money had been lost and he could not compensate for it. In addition to issuing an arrest warrant, the county government is requiring the guarantor to compensate for the funds.

Abduction of a Woman S Sentenced to Imprisonment: Zhang Xiudai, who abducted a woman and was arrested at the No. 1 Hotel in the Xiaoshan city area some time ago, and Wang Meiying, the woman who was abducted from Lin'an, were summoned by Prosecutor Zheng of the county court to have the Wang family from Lin'an come to claim her. Yesterday, the abductor Zhang Xiudai was brought to trial in the First Criminal Court. As a result, Zhang was sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment and five years of deprivation of civil rights for the crime of abducting a woman under the age of twenty.

Fishermen Request Exemption from Fishing Tax: More than ten fishing households, including Cao Bingxian, outside the South Gate of Xiaoshan, are suffering from poor fishing and frequent theft of fresh fish, resulting in unbearable losses. Therefore, they plan to petition the county government to exempt them from the annual fishing tax in accordance with the regulations promulgated by the Civil Affairs Department to maintain the fishing industry. It is not known whether the superiors will approve their request.

Township Offices to Re-elect: Xiaoshan township offices began preparations in May of last year. After following the prescribed procedures, conducting household surveys, and swearing in citizens, each township began elections in December of last year. Just as the elections were about to be completed, a provincial telegram ordered them to stop. Now, another provincial order has instructed that elections be held within July, and that the prior swearing-in of citizens is still valid, but the members of the repair circle elected previously are all invalid.

Letters 54

Letter from the Anhui Xuyi County Party Rectification Committee 55

To the editors of your esteemed newspaper: We have read the article in the "Local News" column of your newspaper on May 15th regarding the arrest of Wu Jingxiu, Hua Kaihao, and others, who are jointly accused in the Xuyi and Sizhou area. The facts are generally correct. Zhang Pengchao has long been a known Communist Party member with evidence against him. During the purge of the party, he secretly returned to Xuyi and relied on the protection of Wu Jingxiu to survive in various government agencies. Later, last year, Hua Kaihao, Lu Xiaogang, and others colluded with a large number of Communist Party members and came to Xuyi to work as teachers. Party members Yang Mengjiu and others obtained substantial evidence and submitted it to the superior party department. Subsequently, the Anhui Provincial Party Department and the Provincial Government separately issued secret orders to the Xuyi County Party Department and the County Government to jointly arrest Zhang Pengchao, Wu Jingxiu, Hua Kaihao, Li Xianying, Lu Xiaogang, Du Zhonghe, and eleven others and send them to the province for legal proceedings. However, the suspects fled upon hearing the news. On March 30th, Tu Jiangong, a detective dispatched by the County Government, arrested Wu Jingxiu and Hua Kaihao at the Zhonghe Hotel in the capital city and has already sent them to the province to await trial. Zhang Pengchao did not turn himself in. Furthermore, we have read a letter from Zhang Pengchao, Wu Jingxiu, Hua Kaihao, and others in the "Local News" column of your newspaper on May 23rd, which is full of false accusations and cunning attempts to escape punishment. It also claims that the County Chamber of Commerce, the County Farmers' Association, the Finance Management Office, district offices, standing troops, and various organizations sent representatives Qin Yangchen, Yang Ruchen, and others to the province to appeal their unjust treatment. This is even more absurd. The County Farmers' Association has not yet been organized. The director of the Finance Management Office was Hua Kaihao. Because no one is in charge, it is still managed by the original staff. The standing troops have already been ordered to be disbanded by the provincial government. Moreover, under party rule, which organizations would dare to betray the party and the country and secretly collude with and protect Communist Party members? Our committee has separately ordered the relevant legal organizations to thoroughly investigate whether they have sent representatives and has also reported to the Provincial Party Department and forwarded the report to the Military Law Tribunal of the Provincial Government for strict prevention of any fraudulent actions. We hereby urge your newspaper to make corrections to maintain the integrity of the party. Dong Zhong, Organizing Committee Member and Training Director.

Educational News

Special Article

Discussing Children's Literature by Shang Zhongyi 56

(Reply to Mr. Wu Yan'yin Again)

After reading Mr. Wu Yan'yin's article in the Shen Bao on May 19th, I feel that Mr. Wu has misunderstood the target of my remarks. I am afraid that my comrades in the field of children's education may be misled and all go astray. Therefore, I hereby clarify my position to dispel any doubts. As for any words that involve emotional disputes, they seem to be outside the scope of academic discussion, so I will not participate in them.

1. Mr. Wu's article says, "After reading Mr. Shang's great work, the atmosphere is very tense, as if the current Chinese primary school textbooks are full of the 'fantastic fairy tales' that Mr. Shang is talking about. In fact, I can comfort Mr. Shang with a joke. Our country's primary school textbooks have never been like American textbooks. There is not much material about 'fantastic fairy tales.' Even if there are some in the national language textbooks, they are minimal. However, I don't think Mr. Shang's remarks are 'shooting at nothing.' Chinese primary school textbooks may be misunderstood in the future and become like American textbooks, full of 'fantastic fairy tales.'"

What Mr. Wu is referring to is my article "On Children's Literature Again." However, the article discusses "children's literature" and not specifically "textbooks."

Now, let's take the commonly circulated national language textbooks as an example, based on thirty volumes (New Era, Volumes 1-8 of the Commercial Press, New School System, Volumes 1-8, and New China, Volumes 1-7 of Zhonghua, and New Primary School, Volumes 1-4, 6-8). An examination of national language textbooks shows that materials that "violate natural phenomena" account for 21% of the total. As for ordinary children's literature, this proportion is likely to be higher. (By the way, newly emerging textbooks in the United States, such as HordyGageHrno's readers, have very few materials that "violate natural phenomena." The readers are not at hand, so I cannot be sure of the exact proportion, but as far as I remember, it is definitely below 21%.)

2. Mr. Wu's article says, "As for those who support 'fantastic fairy tales,' Mr. Shang's paper seems to designate me as one of them. In fact, Mr. Shang has misunderstood me. Although I am not enlightened, I will never be a loyal subject of 'fantastic fairy tales.' I am currently in a hurry to complete a national language textbook for lower grades that is full of new natural events (not avoiding bird and animal language). I don't have time to discuss this matter further. I hope Mr. Shang will not make any more remarks that are not very relevant to this topic, other than the question of whether 'bird and animal language' is the same as ghost stories and should be broken. Otherwise, not only will it be too far from the topic, but I will also not dare to discuss it with Mr. Shang again." When the Children's Education Society discussed the selection of children's literature, I proposed nine negative standards and ten positive standards. "Violating natural phenomena" is one of the negative standards. Cramming nineteen standards into thirty minutes felt like the poem was short but the meaning was long and I could not fully express myself. So, I declared to the crowd, "In the near future, I will have a more detailed and precise discussion to seek correction from you all." At that time, I planned to divide the nineteen standards into several articles, and "On Children's Literature Again" is one of them. It is a sequel that specifically discusses "violating natural phenomena." My previous and subsequent remarks were all aimed at the comrades of the Children's Education Society to provide them with reference and criticism. When I discussed this matter at the Children's Education Society, I did not think of Mr. Wu, and when I published the article, I was only incidentally answering Mr. Wu's questions. The main purpose was still to explain my unfinished thoughts to my comrades and not specifically to Mr. Wu. Mr. Wu believes that I designated him as one of them is a misunderstanding.

3. Mr. Wu says, "If we do not recognize Mr. Shang's lofty arguments and think that Mr. Shang is also opposed to 'cat and dog textbooks,' then textbooks of 'heaven, earth, sun, and moon'... may be revived."

This section does not directly involve me, but I can also take this opportunity to solemnly declare that I am very suspicious and negative about stories and other literature that violate natural phenomena. However, my hope for children's literature is not to return to the past but to go a step further from fairy tales and stories to seek sound and flawless literature that is reasonable and does not violate nature.

4. Mr. Wu asks, "'Is 'bird and animal language' the same as ghost stories and should be broken'?"

The violation of natural phenomena in ghost stories lies in their content, while the violation of nature in stories lies more in their form. Although there are differences in the nature of their violation of natural phenomena, their "violation of natural phenomena" is the same. Regarding this type of literature that violates nature, I have already made a frank statement in my article "On Children's Literature Again." Now, I would like to reiterate: "Instead of using literature that violates nature with questionable value and containing risks, why not use literature that has value and no risks based on facts and possible materials?" (Narrowing its scope, it can specifically refer to stories.) "Instead of using stories with questionable value and containing risks, why not use natural literature that has value and no risks?"

Because the violation of nature in stories is mostly only in form and does not penetrate into the content, the risks it contains may be less than those in ghost stories. For example, I once said during a discussion at the Children's Education Society, "Children have the opportunity to correct themselves if they see cats talking in literature..." Therefore, my attitude towards stories is slightly more tolerant than towards ghost stories. But further asking, "Why give children a concept that still needs to be corrected instead of directly giving them a concept that does not need correction?" So, the question I am currently holding is: "If we can achieve the same (or better) effect without using bird and animal language, while also avoiding the possibility of its risks (at least saving the trouble of correction), why must we use bird and animal language?" If we say that we cannot achieve the same or better effect without using stories, what about the works of Fabre of France and Selon of the United States? The above is from a principled perspective. In reality, I advocate greatly reducing the number of stories in children's literature to make room for sound, flawless, and natural stories and scientific literature that do not violate nature. In principle and in practice, this is my position.

During the discussion at the Children's Education Society, my use of the word "break" was entirely in a joking tone to express my negative attitude towards "violating nature," similar to Mr. Wu's comforting me with a joke. Everyone present that day was able to understand the attitude with which those two words were used. If you think that I should not involve joking in academic discussions, I hereby inform my comrades of this oversight.

But whether or not it is "broken," I am indeed negative and doubtful about all literature that violates nature.

Important News

Zhang, Director of the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education, Resigns Due to Four Months of Teacher Salary Arrears 57

Teachers and Staff Will Strike Due to Wage Arrears

Zhang Daoshen, the director of the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education, has made plans for the progress of education in the province, but he is hampered by a lack of funds and cannot clear the old debt for various educational institutions. It is difficult to maintain existing businesses. He has already submitted his resignation request. I have learned that his submission is as follows:

For the matter of submitting a request, I, Daoshen, have been appointed by the National Government as a member of the Zhejiang Provincial Government and Director of the Department of Education. Since taking office, I have been in office for more than five months. I have tried my best to follow in the footsteps of the previous director, to proceed according to the procedures, and to strive for improvement. However, the implementation of the plan depends on the economy. The officials of the provincial government are well aware of this. I am grateful to Chairman Zhang and Wang Cheng'ying, Director of the Department of Finance, for their consideration of education and their efforts to allocate the necessary funds. However, due to the accumulation of old debts, it is difficult to clear them. The funds for provincial educational institutions have been in arrears for as many as four months since January of this year. The requests for salary payments from various schools arrive day and night, and some even set schedules and demand in various ways. I have observed that, regarding the accumulated expenses, if their requests cannot be met, some teachers and staff who fail to understand the government's difficulties may resort to strikes and work stoppages. The impact is not only related to the future of education in this province but also enough to confuse the views of distant parties. In recent days, those who have come to the department to demand payment have been exhorted by Daofan with righteousness to make things difficult for them. However, the need for funds is imminent, and empty words are ultimately difficult to satisfy their hopes. I humbly believe that the provincial government's financial exhaustion is a fact and cannot be concealed, while the schools' salary arrears of four months of payment also feel very difficult. Daoshen clearly knows that the provincial treasury is like this and it is impossible to urge them to pay. The economic situation of the schools is the same. It is indeed difficult to deal with. Not only is it difficult to implement the new projects planned by this department, but even if we want to slightly rectify the existing businesses, we are limited by the funds that cannot be paid out on a monthly basis, and we cannot proceed. If this continues, it will be difficult to maintain the status quo. I deeply believe that education is the foundation of a nation, while economy is the source of a business. At the beginning of the political training period, we should do our best to build. However, after assessing the situation, even if we think hard about sharing the difficulties and striving to promote progress, it is difficult for a clever woman to cook without rice. After thinking again and again, instead of being unable to develop and being hindered from proceeding, why not let the capable as soon as possible, so as to avoid misleading them? I humbly ask you to examine your sincerity and allow me to forward this to the central government to remove me from my concurrent positions. I am extremely anxious to obey orders. To the best of my knowledge, I submit this to Zhang, Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, and Zhang Daofan, Director of the Department of Education.

Local

Executive Committee of the Joint Association of Vocational Guidance Agencies 59

Important Resolutions: Seven Items Fully Passed

The Second Annual Meeting Will Be Held in Early August

The Second Executive Committee Meeting to Be Held in Jiading

The Shanghai Vocational Guidance Institute, based on the resolution of the 11th annual meeting on July 20, 1920, organized the National Association of Vocational Guidance Agencies of China. It was formally established at a meeting in the institute on September 21, 1920, and a general meeting was held in the capital on December 14, 1920, to discuss 49 important proposals. It is now learned that the association has begun to implement the various proposals separately. The first executive committee meeting was held at the China Vocational Education Society at 10:00 a.m. on May 31 of this year. The proceedings of the meeting are summarized below. Attending Personnel: Xie Yicheng (Nanjing Municipal Vocational Guidance Institute), Chen Qingshi (Great China University), Feng Baoling, Zhu Youqian (Chinese Engineering Society), Yang Zhuofu (Jiading Vocational Guidance Institute), He Qingru (Youth Association), Yang Weiyu (China Vocational Education Society), Zhang Zhong (Provincial Shanghai High School), Xi Junchu (Shanghai University), Gao Jiansi (Provincial Jiangsu Educational Institute), Wu Xixu (Wuxian Vocational Guidance Institute), Pan Yangyao (Shanghai Vocational Guidance Institute), and other eleven executive committee members attended. Dr. He Qingru was publicly elected as chairman.

Reported Matters: Mr. Pan Yangyao reported on his observations of vocational guidance in Japan and reported on the association's work progress and income and expenditure of membership fees. Discussion of Proposals: (1) Draft Measures for the Implementation of Vocational Guidance in Universities, Middle Schools, and Elementary Schools (Resolved): It is requested that the educational administrative authorities issue an order to the principals of schools at all levels to refer to the measures for the implementation of vocational guidance in schools at all levels formulated by the association, and that schools at all levels establish vocational guidance committees to be responsible for the implementation of vocational guidance and to liaise with the association. (2) The association should publish vocational guidance publications to expand vocational education guidance research and publicity and to facilitate the selection of registered talents (Resolved): The association will organize an editorial committee to publish a quarterly and cooperate with major newspapers in Shanghai to publish special vocational guidance publications. Committee members will be appointed to write and edit articles. He Qingru, Chen Qingshi, Zhu Youqian, Zhang Zhong, and Pan Yangyao were immediately appointed as editorial committee members, and Mr. Pan Yangyao was requested to convene a meeting. (3) Efforts should be made to establish vocational supplementary schools or training classes to provide education for unemployed youth (Resolved): The association's agencies in each location will investigate the academic subjects needed for supplementary education in the vocational sector and liaise with local business leaders to request the local education bureau to establish vocational supplementary schools or training classes at minimal cost. (4) The tutor system should be implemented in schools at all levels on a trial basis (Resolved): The association will send separate letters to universities and middle schools to implement it on a trial basis. (5) The association should invite experts to give lectures on vocational guidance in senior middle schools in various provinces (Resolved): The association should introduce experts to give lectures on vocational guidance in junior middle schools in various places at the request of middle schools in various places. (6) Should the location and time of the second annual meeting be predetermined (Resolved): Early August of the 20th year, to be held concurrently with the annual meeting of national vocational education agencies organized by the China Vocational Education Society. (7) Date and location of the association's second executive committee meeting (Resolved): June 28th of the 20th year at 10:00 a.m. in Jiading. The Jiading Vocational Guidance Institute is designated to prepare advance notice.

Statistics on the Number of Chinese Students Studying in the United States from Various Countries 60

Canada is the Most, China is Second

According to news from the travel department of the Chinese Students' Association in Card Road, the number of Chinese students studying in Japan and Europe has increased dramatically in recent years, so the increase in the number of students studying in the United States between 1930 and 1931 is very small. Currently, there are 1,336 Chinese students studying at various universities in the United States, an increase of only 73 from last year's 1,263. Among them, 242 are in New York State, 224 are in California, 155 are in Illinois, and 114 are in Massachusetts. In addition, 601 are in other states. This year, the total number of students studying in the United States from various countries is 10,478, covering 102 nationalities. Canada has the most, with 1,410, followed by China with 1,336, and Japan with 1,004. The above numbers only refer to those studying higher disciplines in specialized schools above the college level in the United States. In addition, there are a few studying in other preparatory schools, so the average estimate of the total number of students studying in the United States from various countries is about 15,000.

The Third District Education Association Protects the Livelihood of Members 61

And Provides Relief to Unemployed Members

The Education Association of the Third District of this city held its fourth executive committee meeting in the association's conference room at 5:00 p.m. yesterday. Xu Huimin, Zhang Tianbai, Chen Jicheng, Tang Liqing, and Yuan Rong attended. Tang Liqing presided over the meeting. Jiaotong Won the Jiangda Baseball Championship Without Effort 68

Fudan Gave Up Due to Freshmen

Friendship Game... Fudan Wins Jiaotong... 15 to 8

The Jiangda baseball game has reached the stage of close combat. In the first battle, Jiaotong defeated Jinan. In the second battle, Jinan defeated Fudan. Yesterday afternoon, Jiaotong met Fudan at the China Baseball Field. When the bell rang three times to declare war, the Jiaotong army had already stationed in the field, preparing for a bloody battle. However, news came that the Fudan players gave up their rights due to the final exam. The Jiaotong baseball team won the championship without losing a soldier or a shot. At that time, because the freshmen in the Fudan team could not participate, they temporarily invited Jiaotong to play a friendly match. After seven innings of fighting, the Jiaotong champion unexpectedly fell under the iron hooves of the new army. This is also an unexpected anecdote. In the first inning, Jiaotong scored two points with two runners returning to base between a wave of their hands. In the second inning, Fudan's safe hits came like a string of beads. By the time Jiaotong reorganized its lineup to make up for the situation, it was already irreversible. In this inning, Fudan gained seven points, and Jiaotong gained one point. In the subsequent three innings, Jiaotong prevented the enemy's progress and tried to find a way out. Under the door, they snatched three points. Unexpectedly, after a little carelessness, the Fudan army invaded again in the sixth and seventh innings, losing a total of eight points, while Jiaotong only scored two points. The result of the friendly match was 15 to 8, Fudan won.
