Free Talk

World Mini-Chronicle 74

— Sea Visitor

There is a noble Bohemian restaurant in Paris where guests must go to the kitchen to cook for themselves. This is absolutely unique among restaurants in various countries.

The wax figures displayed in British department stores are extremely lifelike. All the hair and teeth are made of real materials, so the price is very expensive.

In the past year, the number of passengers carried by all railways in the UK and the London Underground has increased significantly, 40 million more than in 1928.

There is a hermit in Korea who does not eat cooked food every day, but only eats water and three pine nuts. It is said that he can live to be two hundred years old.

Windsor House, a mansion in London, is the detached palace of the British royal family. The palace contains a large number of clocks, a total of 360, and there is an initially manufactured lever watch, which is a rare antique.

The newly elected French President Doumer has four sons who all sacrificed for the country in the European War. The Paris city authorities specially named a street (Paul Doumer's Four Sons Street) in memory.

The interior of Westminster Cathedral in London will be redecorated entirely with exquisite mosaic work, costing one million pounds and taking two hundred years to complete.

Dust Talk from the Finger Zen Room 75

— Jing Mengdie

South of the Yangtze River, those who speak of Chinese medicine unanimously recommend Mr. He Jiheng of Danyang. Mr. He is over sixty years old, but he is energetic and talkative, and looks like he is in his forties. From this, it can be seen that he has mastered the art of health preservation. He is proficient in calligraphy and literature, and is a doctor who is also a Confucian. He named his residence the Finger Zen Room, meaning that the Bodhisattva manifested himself with great wisdom. The small room is the Vimalakirti's abbot, freely using his samadhi in a finger Zen machine, so he can make every move successful and become a lucky star and a living Buddha for thousands of families. I once participated in the treatment of diseases and recognized Mr. He, and I received his great favor and made a friendship that transcends age. However, we have not seen each other for several years. Last Sunday, I took my sick wife to Dancheng again. It was already dark and there was a heavy storm, so I left my wife in the inn and went alone to knock on Mr. He's door. When I opened the door and entered, we were surprised and delighted to see each other. He said that I came in the deep night and heavy storm, and my feelings were no less than those of Wang Ziyou, who visited Dai An Daikui in Shanyin on a snowy day. There were already three guests in the room, and Mr. He introduced them to me one by one, saying that they were all scholars. I smiled and said, "How can there be vulgar guests in this room?" The night rain in Bashan, the old story by the west window, the tea smoke is green, and the lamp flower is not red. Outside the curtain, I no longer know the bell ringing and the leakage is exhausted. The guests left in the middle of the night, but I stayed alone, and the secluded interest was not yet exhausted, and the high talk turned clear. Mr. He said that my country's medicine began to decline when Ye Tianshi came out, not because Ye's art was sparse, but because those who studied Ye's art were at fault. The ancient doctors were all practical and laid a solid foundation. Ye was born with a genius, but he took the path of ingenuity and took shortcuts. Like a military strategist, he was determined to win by using partial divisions and strange plans, and no longer saw the dignified drums and the upright flags. Later scholars followed the trend and changed their practices. Without Ye's cleverness, they only took advantage of his quick effects. Whether it was playing cleverness and hurting the patient's family, they had already lost the ancient people's sincere and fearless model. Every situation was getting worse, and the medical way was no longer able to be asked. I said that this theory can be applied to poetry. The existence of Ye in medicine is like the existence of Suiyuan in poetry. Suiyuan specializes in spirituality in poetry and does not take style. His theory is convenient for beginners and teaches people to use skill, but the mellow flavor before the Tang Dynasty is all gone. Moreover, scholars without his talent and who imitate his poems are more likely to flow into the disease of frivolousness. It is also like the modern painter Wu Changshuo, who opened the door of sparseness and strength for the younger generation, but nowadays there are many rough and expanded works. This is all the same as the advantages and disadvantages of Ye's medical benefits. Mr. He looked at each other and laughed when he heard the words, but the bell on the wall had already reported three times, so we cherished each other and parted and returned to Xihou to write it.

Singing Aloud After Being Drunk, Written to Show Da Ke, Lv Chen, Zhu Ming and Other Gentlemen with a Smile 76

— Gu Foying

The old man Hai Cang read my poems and said that I am outstanding and extraordinary. How can there be no two or three people in Jiangnan who are like me? Once a fine horse comes out, they will all be defeated. How many confidants have I known in my life? (Borrowing the sentence from Hai Cang) The public said that I am happy, but the world is suspicious. Stop, stop, the world should not be suspicious. The gentleman spit out the wonders in his chest that can make you twitch your tongue and stare your eyes. He learned to read without a teacher, and the alaya consciousness is his teacher. The gentleman also has no servants or concubines, and the flower demon and tree spirit are available for driving. However, the gentleman is still a human being in the world. The gentleman knows the bitterness and suffering in the world. It is not enough to talk about birth, old age, sickness, and death. The most unbearable thing is to seek what cannot be obtained and to love and separate. What does the gentleman love? All sentient beings are like his wife. What does the gentleman seek? He only seeks to help all sentient beings ascend to the ladder to heaven one by one. The psychologist Freud heard it and said: "Although this is just a change of sexuality, the source of world culture and art lies in this." The gentleman laughed loudly and suddenly. He only saw the youthful daylight flying in the air, suddenly like a current of electricity running through all the veins, and like the smell of alcohol reaching the limbs, like a crazy tide rising and shaking the chest and armpits, like a demon snake entering and accumulating the heart and spleen, like truth and illusion, like a dream, like sorrow, like anger, like thirst and hunger. The heavenly swan and the imperial girl hid and peeped at the door, and the auspicious unicorn and the phoenix came one after another. The great bright lamp was hanging high, and the mandala flowers were piled up on the steps. Lao Zhuang Qu Song dedicated their pens and inks, and Su Huang Li Du opened their zuns and yis. The Western Shaw Bonner and the Eastern Tagore, the old servants follow left and right. The gentleman drank ten thousand zhis of pain, and the falling paper was so smooth that each word was like a flower, and each word was like the sun and the moon hanging down. The vitality of the universe was released, and then there was the gentleman's poem. Alas, then there was the gentleman's poem in the world.

Feelings from Watching "The Sea of Regret" 77

— Tu Nan

Opium and prostitution are fierce weapons that cripple the youth's body and ruin their future. Promising citizens are destroyed by them beyond recognition. It can be said that even children with a little knowledge know the harm of these two things. However, judging from the current society, I don't know how many people knowingly commit crimes, are confused for a while, and regret it for the rest of their lives. Only when their money is exhausted and they have no face as heroes do they realize and regret it, but it is already too late. Therefore, the government has repeatedly ordered the prohibition of opium and prostitution. However, if you look at it with sharp eyes, those who prohibit it will prohibit it, and those who commit it will commit it. It is just like a piece of paper that has nothing to do with them. Some people say that it is not necessary to strictly prohibit it. It is better to collect taxes in the prohibition, which is more effective and visible. However, this is a passive method. It is better to use a kind of edification method to approach, which should be superficial and practical, so that a group of friends who are addicted can automatically realize it without knowing it. Then, although the mulberry tree is lost, there is still a corner to the east. After talking about it, I want to talk about movies. The edification power of movies is very great, and it is easier than various kinds of publicity. After watching "The Sea of Regret" recently released by the Star Film Company, I felt the above remarks. "The Sea of Regret" was originally a narrative of an old novel from decades ago, and it was also a matter of decades ago. However, the harm of being harmed by opium and prostitutes is described very vividly and deeply. After reading it, it can indeed make people wake up. The Chen Boh of the drama can be said to be too many people in the current society who have the same disease as him. After reading the result of Chen Boh's, we young people are really in great danger. People who are not deeply involved in the world, I dare to introduce you to see it, especially in the government, we should encourage film companies to produce more films of this kind, then its effect may be more practical than a piece of paper.

A Small Record of the Treasures of Chengyuan Garden 78

— Huo Gong

Pan Zhang Chengbo has been the Chinese manager of the Yihuo Shipping Company for decades. He is now old and unable to cope with the arduous work. He has handed over the company's affairs to Wen Lang Zhiquan. He plans to take a long-term trip to Europe and the United States. All the antiques, treasures, jewels, and furnishings purchased over the years in Chengyuan Garden at No. 2 Gelo Road will be transferred together to facilitate his departure. After arriving in Europe and the United States, if he encounters a suitable location, he will build a villa there as a place for entertaining the elderly. If he returns to China, he should run another rabbit fur coat to enjoy his remaining years. The most valuable of the items he is currently planning to transfer are the ancient bronze bells, tripods, yis, jués, and incense burners from the Xia, Shang, Zhou, Qin, and Han dynasties; the incense boxes of the Qing Yongzheng dynasty; the flower vases of the Kangxi dynasty; the flower pots of the Qianlong Kiln; the white jade ruyis; the jadeite water containers; the ivory carved screens for palace use; the rosewood inlaid jade screens and hanging screens; the natural boats, mountains, water, and inserted tablets; the authentic calligraphy and paintings of famous people from past dynasties; various rosewood, shade wood, teak, and mahogany large armchairs and master chairs; natural tables, offering tables, Eight Immortals tables, antique cabinets, flower stands, piano platforms, tea platforms, marble pit beds, imported carriage materials, glass ware, cream lacquer rooms, colors, Beijing carpets, gold thread table carpets, various silverware, alum stone floor lamps, potted flowers, etc. There are all kinds of things, and those who have the same interests can go to Chengyuan Garden to take a look on Wednesday, Thursday, and Friday of this week.

Around the Yellow Sea (20) 79

— Huang Yanpei

In Anjo Town, I saw two very tall and large wooden plaques inscribed with "Hekikai County Reservists Association" and "Anjo Town Youth Corps". The regulations of the Youth Corps are slightly different across Japan, but every city, town, and village organizes one because it is mandated by the government and national policy, holding great significance. They are not allowed to not organize one. Some regulations stipulate an age range from teens to early twenties, while others require a certain level of education, such as graduation from a specific type of school. How do they ensure everyone joins? Normally, military service requires two years, but Youth Corps members only need one and a half years. Soldiers are divided into upper, middle, and lower ranks, progressing sequentially, but Youth Corps members can jump directly to the upper rank, so everyone wants to join. How are they taught? (1) Physical training (2) Character training (3) Vocational training. I have already mentioned that. Ultimately, why do they exert such great effort and organize the Youth Corps on such a large scale? What is the reason? To be frank, it is to prepare for war. Who will they fight? It is rumored to be a certain country. Why would they involve my country? What is the ultimate cause? What piece of land is at stake? I hope all my fellow countrymen will think about it.

Why is the Youth Corps related to warfare? It is because they prepare various military strategies, defense, military supplies, and so on. However, they always feel that the population is too small. If they rely on each individual to risk their lives, it might not be enough. The only way to win against a larger force is to have a smaller but highly skilled army. Besides active duty soldiers, there are reserves and continuing reserves. What comes after that? If every young person from their teens to their early twenties is thoroughly trained and qualified to serve as a reserve for the reserves, then they will have nothing to fear. Moreover, by uniting these young people across the country, it becomes easy to instill any ideology or rally them against any enemy. How profound and ruthless is their intention?

Therefore, the Youth Corps must also be linked to the Reservists Association, so that the older generation can lead the younger generation.

The Anjo Youth Corps uses five ordinary elementary schools as its center, but students from higher elementary schools and supplementary schools can also join, regardless of gender. The town mayor serves concurrently as the corps leader. This is what the school principal told me.

Hearing this, one might feel that the Hekikai countryside is filled with a murderous aura. Not at all! Please look at a notice at Anjo Station:

Nagoya Railway Bureau Notice: Cherry Blossom Viewing Information

Thursday, April 16th

Ueno Park: Full bloom; Koganei: 70%

Mount Yoshino: Upper: 70%; Middle: 80%; Lower: 50%; Arashiyama embankment: Soon to bloom

Yoro Park: 60%

Their railway authorities are so conscientious, so interesting, and so willing to take care of the common people. No wonder their people are so refined. The old woman at the Western-style restaurant drooled when she talked about cherry blossom viewing...

I shout two slogans for them: "Love your country without being frivolous; enjoy the cherry blossoms without forgetting to love your country!"

Rotary Club Speech

Random Thoughts on the Lake (1) 80

— Tianxu Wosheng

The water of West Lake has recently become incredibly polluted, unfit not only for drinking but also for washing. After drawing water, adding alum, and allowing it to settle overnight, the next morning, when boiling it for cooking, reddish crystals are immediately seen floating and sinking, almost filling the pot, which is disgusting. Therefore, I fetch water from Jade Spring day and night, but the water taken from the pond by the stele is still clear; even the water in the fish pond is turbid and unpleasant. If I were to fetch water from Tiger Spring, it would cost one yuan for every two buckets, enough for only three days of cooking. West Lake used to have a Lotus Wine Courtyard in Jinsha Ravine, where lotus flowers were grown, hence the Lotus Wine Courtyard, which was used to brew wine. Zhou Zizhi discussed moving the Lotus Wine Courtyard with Minister Zhang, writing that the Ministry of Revenue had the Lotus Wine Courtyard in West Lake for six or seven years, yielding over six million catties of lotus roots, from which the government profited over 300,000 strings of cash. Some people proposed moving it, not knowing that both wine and lotus roots require water, and good water makes them excellent, while bad water ruins them. One must choose carefully. West Lake's water was once as clear as sugar. Now, the proposed new location is near a turbid harbor, using bamboo pipes to draw river water from less than a hundred feet away, flowing with the tide. Its taste is very poor. They are unwilling to dig wells for spring water, not realizing that the source of the spring is also the tide. Furthermore, Su Shi requested permission to dredge West Lake, stating that no official wine production in the world was as large as Hangzhou's, with annual taxes of over 200,000 strings of cash, relying on the lake for water. If the lake gradually shrinks and the water does not flow properly, people will have to fetch mountain spring water from afar, costing no less than 200,000 workdays per year. This shows how important the purity of the lake water is. Even if the people of Hangzhou do not brew wine, they all buy it from Shaoxing. Yet, rinsing caps and washing feet in the lake inevitably brings criticism from all over, who all view it as if it were the Yellow River and lament that no sage is emerging. In my opinion, algae in the lake are a major cause of the sediment that makes it turbid. Only large fish can eat algae, and among fish, the longest-lived and easiest to breed are carp. Therefore, the people of Hangzhou pretend to follow the teachings of the gods and prohibit eating carp, claiming that April 8th is Buddha's birthday and encouraging people to release carp into West Lake, perhaps as a remnant of Fan Zhongyan's policy of using the ignorance of the people. Algae ash is rich in potassium carbonate. Last winter, I saw piles of it near Bai Causeway, as if someone were collecting it and drying it for fuel. If so, then using the ash as fertilizer for fish farming, or using lye made from the ash for washing clothes, is also a proper use and not a waste.

Willow catkins can turn into duckweed. On sunny and windless days in February, willow cotton clings to the trees, resembling a graceful maiden wearing a crane cloak by the lake. When the east wind suddenly rises, it flies across the lake, turning the entire surface white like snow. Overnight, it turns yellowish-green, floating on the water like moss. Much of the lake's turbidity is due to this. Fish accidentally eat it, only to spit it out. Jade Spring uses rice cakes to feed the fish. When the cakes float on the surface, the fish compete to eat them, often splashing around, making for an enjoyable sight. However, when willow catkins fill the water, turning it green, the fish mostly hide and only eat the cakes after they sink. The knowledge of fish is also remarkable. The Central Health Department once prohibited adding salicylic acid to soy sauce to prevent mold because it hinders digestion. Fish can protect their own lives in this way, showing that humans are not as good as birds, and certainly not as good as fish.

Gold Market Advances Eight Hundred Taels Mark 81

Fluctuating unpredictably and ultimately plunging sharply. Yesterday, the gold price fell again, breaking through the 800-tael mark. The market chaos is ultimately unstoppable. The waves surge, and people are panic-stricken. The situation is particularly precarious. The overall market had a difference of eighteen or nineteen taels, ultimately plunging thirteen taels, reversing several days of consecutive gains. There were more sellers, but receipts and payments were divergent. The silver market continued to rise, opening low, then rising as buyers became active, and it was rumored that the U.S. stock market had fallen, briefly breaking through 810 taels. Afterwards, the foreign exchange rate increased by half a notch, and the domestic market also hardened, with major players dumping their holdings in a rapid retreat, falling sharply by more than ten taels. The price then suddenly broke through 800 taels, hovering around that mark. Later, selling pressure surged, and the exchange rate declined further, making the market extremely weak and in a state of rapid decline. A sharp drop of eight or nine taels was expected if the silver market continued to rise. The silver price continued to rise, opening lower. The opening price for the early July contract fell by two or three mace to 806 taels 1 mace. Because major silver firms all increased by one-sixteenth, the silver price increased by eight fen three li. Private telegrams added one-sixteenth. Shortly after, it fell again to 805 taels 5 mace. Then, Yuan Mao Yong, Yuan Kang, Xiang Wanxing, Shunli, and others all sold off, and British gold from various banks initially traded at 1/2/1/125. Then, at 2 pence 0.0625, it immediately rose sharply to 811 taels 5 mace. Afterwards, downstream sellers such as Taichang, Yuanheng, Zhifeng, Yong, and others came in to sell, and British gold could be settled at 2 pence 0.0625 to 125, now falling back to 0.08 taels 2 mace. The increase momentarily jumped three taels to 11 taels 13 mace, with Dadecheng, Hengyu, and others joining in the selling. Furthermore, Mitsui and HSBC sold British gold at 2 pence 0.0625, seeming to stabilize. The initial orders were announced, increasing by 125. U.S. gold fell by 1.5 fen, suppressing the price to 10 taels, then 0.09 taels 2 mace 3 li. Soon after, Qian Changxiang, Dadecheng, Yuan Kangxiang, Zhifeng, Yonghengxing, and others all sold off. Furthermore, fellow traders converted British gold into silver, with banks taking 25. As a result, the gold price fell by more than 6 taels, and at 10:30, it was only 0.03 taels 3 mace. Strong Sales of Cotton Yarn to the North 86

Actual sales of cotton yarn are increasingly active. Purchasing from the Tianjin area in the north is particularly enthusiastic. Furthermore, Jinan and Xuzhou in Shandong are also active. This is entirely due to the tightening of exchange rates, preventing the import of Japanese yarn. Furthermore, the local factories in Qingdao have a severe shortage of 16-count and 20-count yarn, and prices are high. Shanghai is over ten taels. Merchants from Tianjin, due to the improved cloth business there, are shipping goods to Mongolia and Tibet for sale. Therefore, the momentum of searching for and purchasing cotton yarn in Shanghai is exceptionally strong, and several factories have had their goods emptied. They are switching to purchasing futures. However, due to high raw material prices, the factories are unwilling to sell off their stock, which shows the strength of the merchants' buying volume. In recent days, exports of cotton yarn have been approximately 30,000 bales. The current market situation is still stable because a high price puts pressure on sellers, and the political situation is unstable with overseas cotton not performing well, so there are many short sellers. However, the actual demand is extremely strong, and bottom stocks are significantly reduced. If there are no special changes in the future, the price of 167-8 taels will likely be realized one day.

The people's price fell and then rose. The people's price on the exchange opened lower due to the poor performance of U.S. cotton and the slight slowdown in sales of spot yarn, each falling 2-5-7 qian. In the afternoon, it was heard that business was booming again in various regions, and the market suddenly strengthened, with each rising 2-3 qian. Transactions totaled 39,200 bales. Grain: The Rice Market at Hexia (Downriver) Becomes Increasingly Slack 89

At the Xinzha (New Gate) rice market in Zhabei yesterday, due to the clear weather, transactions felt even more sluggish. Although there were still many people at the market in the morning, their appetite ultimately seemed sporadic. The market found it difficult to return to high prices. The top-grade, thick "geng" rice (non-glutinous japonica rice) saw no change. The middle and second grades only fell by a few cents. Rice for rice cakes and dumplings sold well, so the price rose by ten cents. The sales of early rice were minimal, and the price neither rose nor fell. "Yangdu" and "Bu" pointed rice were affected by foreign rice, and the opening price fell by five cents. Distilleries only bought a limited amount, so the overall market trended lower. According to news from the miscellaneous grain association, a Taikoo (Butterfield & Swire) company steamer brought 100,000 bags of Saigon rice, priced at eleven yuan and thirty cents. Local purchases were still active, and the opening price was lowered by ten cents.

Standard Flour Plummets by Four Cents 90

Yesterday, the flour market showed a uniform trend of sharp decline. The reason for this heart-stirring event was entirely due to the good weather, which was conducive to wheat harvesting. The collection in various parts of Jiangnan is in full swing, and it is estimated that it will be fully collected in another ten days. Given the current weather, there is a real hope for prolonged sunshine. Therefore, the hearts of people inside and outside the industry are changing. Even the attitude of the mainland traders, which was previously unusually firm, has recently softened. Therefore, from the opening to the close, although the factories did not have a large number of files released, those who returned were seen in layers, causing the market to be unusually dim and the price to gradually fall sharply. Judging from this, because the people's hearts have changed, we still see continued fatigue. As a result, this month fell three cents and two and a half points more than the previous day, July fell three cents and seven and a half points, August fell four cents and two and a half points, September fell three cents, October fell three cents and two and a half points, and November fell three cents and two and a half points.

People's hearts were already temporarily in the air, and they took the opportunity to frantically suppress. For example, English steel plate, flat white iron, corrugated iron, French Western nails, etc. Therefore, the transaction has improved a lot. Although the opening market price has not yet been implemented compared to the negotiated price, it feels much stronger than the previous market. Local News

Commemoration of June 3rd Today 98

Time: 10:00 AM

Location: Municipal Chamber of Commerce

The June 3rd Commemoration in this city has been jointly prepared by the Shanghai Special City Party Department, the Shanghai Municipal Government, and the Chinese National Anti-Opium Association. It will be solemnly held today at 10:00 AM in the Grand Auditorium of the Tianhougong Bridge Municipal Chamber of Commerce. Previously, the Shanghai June 3rd Commemoration Preparatory Committee sent letters to various organizations in this city, requesting them to nominate four representatives to participate. All district branches and bureaus directly under the municipal government have been notified by their respective higher-level party departments and government to attend today to show their respect. The association's news is compiled as follows:

Notice to All Sectors: We are writing to inform you that June 3rd this year marks the 92nd anniversary of the passing of Lin Zexu. To expand publicity, our association, in conjunction with the Shanghai City Party Department, the Municipal Government, and the Chinese National Anti-Opium Association, has decided to hold a commemorative ceremony for opium prohibition at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce at 10:00 AM on June 3rd. In addition to requesting the various district party departments and bureaus directly under the Municipal Government to send personnel through their respective higher-level party departments and organizations, we are writing to respectfully request that you nominate four representatives to attend and participate to show your respect and promote this cause. We would be immensely grateful. We respectfully wish you well.

Publicity Outline: (1) The Significance of the June 3rd Commemoration: Opium importation marked the beginning of political and economic aggression by imperialists against our country. It was also the starting point for the impoverishment of the people and the decline of the nation. Tracing back to the late Qing Dynasty, the British, disregarding humanitarianism, imported opium into the Central Plains, intending to drain our country's wealth and destroy our national vitality. Officials and scholars were unaware of its harm, and addiction became widespread, plunging people into darkness. Not only were individuals harmed by the scourge of drugs, but the country and society also suffered immense losses. Throughout the country, some even took pride in smoking opium, resulting in a century-long legacy of poison and immense suffering. Lin Zexu, realizing the British conspiracy to poison China with drugs, was determined to eliminate the scourge. Therefore, he wrote to the Qing court, vehemently denouncing its harm and taking decisive measures to deal with it. He ordered British merchants to surrender over 20,000 chests of opium and, on this day ninety-two years ago, destroyed them all at Humen, Guangzhou, to demonstrate our country's spirit of opium prohibition and deter the British merchants' audacity in spreading poison. The people were overjoyed.

Eradicate Evil Completely - Respectfully Inscribed by Zhang Qun

The British were quick to send troops, but Lin Zexu's defense was so skillful that they could find no opening. They then attacked Dinghai, Zhejiang, and other coastal areas. Local officials were negligent in their defense, leading to the loss of territory and indemnities, marking the beginning of unequal treaties and plunging our country into an abyss of suffering. The Qing court, unaware of the facts, blamed Lin Zexu for causing trouble by burning opium. Although Lin Zexu's determination to prohibit opium was not fully realized, his courageous spirit of resistance has become an immortal legacy. The National Government, to commemorate the legacy of its predecessors and encourage future generations, has designated this day as our country's Opium Prohibition Commemoration Day, requiring all agencies throughout the country to hold ceremonies. At a time when the aggression of the powers is increasing day by day and the harm of opium continues to grow, we must commemorate the fundamental starting point of the war on opium if we are to abolish all unequal treaties. (1) We should have awareness and effort. Lin Zexu stated in his memorial to the Qing court that "the harm of opium is worse than floods and fierce beasts. Future generations will never consider opium as something that does not need to be prohibited. If this scourge is not eliminated, in ten years there will be no usable soldiers and no funds to be raised. The spread of opium in the interior is like a festering sore on the human body. When a festering sore develops, it gradually produces pus. When opium comes, it gradually leads to bandits. Opium must be completely eliminated to eradicate the root of the disease." This shows that Lin Zexu's observation of the opium scourge was far superior to others. It is a pity that the Qing government was weak, its military preparedness was lax, and it was unable to fight. Moreover, officials and scholars were deeply addicted to opium, and they considered Lin Zexu's actions to be wrong, demanding compensation from Britain and suing for peace, resulting in a century of poison. Since the Republic, local warlords have guarded their own territories, collected opium taxes, forced farmers to plant opium, and protected its trafficking, unknowingly causing countless compatriots to be ruined by the black scourge. The import of foreign drugs has continued unabated. For example, according to the national customs statistics in the nineteenth year of the Republic, seized opium imports reached 32,303 pounds, morphine 1,590 pounds, and cocaine 1,260 pounds. The number of imports that were not seized is even more unknown. The amount of opium planted domestically is even harder to estimate. Today marks the 92nd anniversary of Lin Zexu's burning of opium. Looking back, the opium scourge in our country is still rampant. How can our compatriots not feel pain and vow to completely eradicate it? Fortunately, the anti-opium movement has been developing for years, and opium prohibition laws have long been promulgated. If we can unite as a nation to eliminate opium, it will not be difficult. It is essential to continue the spirit of resistance to opium of the late martyr Lin Zexu and actively participate in the anti-opium movement. Internally, we must urge the government to implement opium prohibition, and externally, we must resist the import of foreign drugs, so that we will not fail Lin Zexu's original aspiration to prohibit opium, and the significance of this commemoration will be immortal.

Agenda: (1) Opening (2) Presidium Takes Seats (3) Play Music and Sing the Party Song (Public Security Bureau Band) (4) Bow Three Times to the Party Flag, National Flag, and Sun Yat-sen's Portrait (5) Bow Three Times to Lin Zexu's Portrait (6) The Chairman Respectfully Reads Sun Yat-sen's Will and Anti-Opium Instructions (7) Three Minutes of Silence (8) Opening Address (9) Report on the Opium Prohibition Situation (Municipal Public Security Bureau) (10) Report on the Anti-Opium Movement in the Past Year (Anti-Opium Association) (11) Speech (12) Oath (13) Play Music (14) Photography (15) Adjournment

Anti-Opium Declaration, June 3rd Commemoration Day, Republic of China, Year 20: Lin Zexu's burning of opium on June 3rd is the most memorable day in our country's history, and it is also a day that all our nationals should never forget. At that time, the British were importing large quantities of opium into China, and its harm was unstoppable. At that time, Lin Wen-zhong alone had the foresight to repeatedly petition the authorities, vehemently denouncing the harm of opium with earnest words. The authorities indeed listened to him and sent him south to investigate opium. After Lin took office as the Governor-General of Guangdong and Guangxi, he ordered the British merchants residing in Guangdong to surrender their stored opium within three days. For a time, it was carried out with great force, and the British did not dare to disobey, so they had to surrender all of it, totaling more than 2.3 million catties. Lin then ordered it to be burned at Humen. It took more than twenty days to burn all of the opium. After the opium was burned, the British leader Elliot was very unwilling and sent many warships to attack Guangdong several times, but Lin Zexu defeated them all. Seeing that there was no opportunity in Guangdong, the British turned to attack Dinghai and Ningbo in Zhejiang, and then crossed the ocean to attack Tianjin, causing shock along the coast and in the capital. The officials were unable to find a way to deal with it and said that Lin Zexu had caused the trouble. Everyone spoke ill of him, and the authorities dismissed him and demoted him to Yili. The Opium War ended there. The Qing Dynasty signed a treaty with the British, paying 6 million yuan in opium indemnity and giving Hong Kong to them. From then on, opium poisoned the whole country until now. When we recall this painful history and look at the harm of opium in China, we cannot help but feel that our responsibility is great and our work is difficult. In the ninety-two years since Lin's failure, foreigners have not only continued to transport opium to China but have also jointly carried out military, economic, and cultural aggression against our country. Fellow comrades,

Please fill out the oath and cut it off together with the mailing address and send it to the Chinese National Anti-Opium Association at No. 4 Ganglu Road, Shanghai. We will send you exquisite anti-opium publications (please enclose 4 cents for postage).

Anti-Opium Oath

I will never plant, produce, transport, sell, or use opium or narcotic drugs, and I will strive to support the anti-opium movement. This oath is sworn on June 3rd, Republic of China, Year 2. Signature of the person taking the oath.

The people of China are groaning under the oppression of the powers. In the final analysis, the root cause is the Opium War. We only need to carefully study why Lin Wen-zhong did not ultimately achieve victory. It was not because he lacked perseverance but because there were no comrades who could continue his aspirations. Because there was no organized group, such a great undertaking relied entirely on his personal spirit and perseverance. Therefore, after he lost power, the anti-opium cause also stopped. This is the only reason for the failure of the anti-opium movement ninety-two years ago, and it is also the only reason for the failure of the anti-opium movement for the past ninety-two years. Since we have realized this, our anti-opium comrades throughout the country must unite and fight together. Although the National Government has repeatedly issued strict orders to ban opium, there are still many soldiers in various provinces who are forcing the people to plant opium and protecting the transportation of opium. Foreign narcotic drugs are still secretly imported continuously, and the proposal for opium sales is still widespread. Under this situation, we should unite and join the National Anti-Opium Movement to be the backing for thorough opium prohibition, so that the opium scourge in the country will be completely eliminated from now on. Everyone should continue the great aspirations of Lin Wen-zhong ninety-two years ago, so that this June 3rd Commemoration Day will not pass in vain. Now the National Government has stipulated that today is the Opium Prohibition Commemoration Day, and for the past two years, the whole country has been vigorously celebrating it. This is the only Commemoration Day for our anti-opium comrades throughout the country. We should work even harder to continue Lin's legacy and thoroughly eradicate all drug scourges. Although Lin Wen-zhong died unfulfilled, his spirit and fearless anti-opium spirit will forever remain in the hearts of everyone in the Chinese nation. He is the vanguard of the anti-opium movement in China. His great spirit and personality are what we should recognize. This is the greatest contribution of the June 3rd Commemoration to us. We hereby declare.

The Situation of Opium Seedlings in Various Provinces in the Past Three Years: The trend of opium seedling planting in our country from the 14th to the 17th year of the Republic of China has gradually spread from the famous opium producing provinces of Yunnan, Guizhou, and Sichuan to the whole country. According to a survey in the 16th year, there was almost no province without opium seedlings, and many provinces competed with each other to increase production. The military and political authorities in various provinces were also in a period of turmoil. The internal war was not peaceful, so they took this opportunity to collect taxes. The people suffered greatly and complained. There were even major changes caused by the collection of opium seedling taxes, resulting in loss of life, such as the resistance of bandits in western Henan and the械鬭of villagers in southern Fujian. Many records of blood and tears can be found in past opium scourge yearbooks. The situation from the winter of 1928 to today is slightly better than before, but although the central government has strict prohibitions, most provinces have not followed them, so opium seedlings have flourished again in northern Anhui, southern Fujian, western Henan, and eastern Shanxi, and Yunnan, Guizhou, and Sichuan are even worse. According to the continuous investigation of our association in the 17th and 18th years of the Republic of China, the number of opium seedlings eradicated in various provinces resulted in 36 counties implementing the eradication of opium seedlings in the 252 county reports in the 17th year of the Republic of China. In the 18th year of the Republic of China (1929), 72 counties implemented the eradication of opium seedlings in the 340 county governments. A brief table can be listed as follows:

Province Republic of China Year 17 Republic of China Year 18 Zhejiang 3,122.0

Henan 2,582.3 3,782.0 Shandong 109.0

Jiangsu 332.4 91.2 Jilin 3,269.0 242.0 Hebei 5 7.2 Shaanxi 57.4 258.4 Hunan 3,370.0 447.0 Guangxi 7.0

Ningxia 13.0 117.5 Ningxia 7.515.5

Yunnan 688.0 846.0 Anhui 125.0 Jiangxi 1.0 Shanxi 0.0 Fujian 2.0 Gansu

Sichuan 70.0 Guangdong 530.0 Hubei 20.0 Heilongjiang 22.0 Chahar 258.9 Xinjiang 120.5 Statistics 21,0665 6,955.3 mu According to the above statistics, almost no province in the country does not find opium seedlings, and the number of counties that eradicated opium seedlings in the 18th year of the Republic of China doubled compared with the 17th year, but the amount of eradication decreased by 33%. The reason may be that the eradication is not strong, or both must be one. As for the planting status of various provinces in recent years, it can be briefly described as follows: (1) Henan, Shaanxi, and Gansu, which have become famine-stricken, believe that the famine in Henan, Shaanxi, and Gansu, which is rare in the past 100 years, chewing grass and cannibalizing people to fill a hungry stomach is unbearable to witness. However, the reason is that the fertile land in the three provinces is mostly planted with opium, resulting in a reduction in agricultural production and a lack of food. According to the experience of the China Foreign Relief Association, in the past, famine relief only required silver coins to be remitted to the disaster area, and food could be purchased from various provinces. Now, it is not the case. The required grains must be directly transported to be sufficient. Because these provinces usually plant too much opium, the production of food is reduced. Once a famine occurs, even if there are millions of gold coins, it is difficult to obtain a large amount of millet and wheat to save them. This is truly heartbreaking and can realize the great harm of planting opium. According to the investigation of our association, the Drug Administration Bureau of Henan Province clearly is an agency for collecting opium taxes. It was cancelled in the 17th year of the Republic of China and restored in the 19th year. This agency collects opium seedling tax of 8 to 15 yuan per mu. Opium seedlings are rarely found in counties near Zhengzhou and Kaifeng. Opium is also planted in rural Luoyang. As for other counties such as Biyang, Luoning, Luoshan, Weishi, Mengxian, and Xinxiang, opium seedlings have not been eradicated in the territory. As for the planting and tax collection of opium in Shaanxi and Gansu provinces, the situation is similar, but the transportation is more inconvenient than in Henan, and more opium is planted for transportation. Xia (as in the original) county in Shaanxi reported that more than 7,000 mu of land were planted with opium and paid land tax, and the land tax was more than 13 yuan per mu. The other counties can be known. In Gansu, the opium tax was 150,000 yuan last year (19th year), and it was increased by 150,000 yuan again last year (19th year). Based on this, it can be inferred that the number of opium planting should be no less. (2) Shandong, where bandits are rampant: At the time of the May 3rd Massacre, the Japanese army forcibly occupied Jinan and seized political power, resulting in the growth of bandits in the northeastern counties of Shandong Province. The opium legacy of the warlord era was taken over by the bandits to collect taxes and could not be eradicated. After the recovery of Jinan, the provincial government unified, but the vitality was lost and it was difficult to suppress bandits. Recently, although the Shandong Provincial Government issued a strict prohibition on opium planting, the government's decrees still do not reach the land where bandits and the Red Spear Society are prevalent, and the people still plant opium without fear. (3) Hubei and Hunan, which have special taxes: Hubei and Hunan provinces were originally opium-free areas, and they have never planted opium. One is that they are not afraid of this, and the other is that they do not need to seek it from afar because they are close to Sichuan, Yunnan, and Kunming. According to the survey in 1929, opium seedlings were also found, but there were very few. Because the special tax relationship between the two lakes is very large, the income from the soil tax and opium tax that passes through the Han River is very large, so the seedling tax is not levied. In this special tax area of the two lakes, the two provincial governments completely ignore the opium prohibition and do not interfere with the discovery of opium seedlings. The areas where they are found are mostly farmers who spontaneously receive bribes from local officials, but they mostly focus on the transportation of opium and do not pay attention to the planting of opium. (4) Guangdong and Guangxi, where opium prohibition has been abolished: Guangdong originally had opium donations as the largest source of income for various miscellaneous taxes, and it has not been abolished yet. The name of the Opium Prohibition Bureau also exists, and the wind of opium smoking is very popular, so the demand for opium is also very high. However, there are very few opium seedlings planted. According to the survey, it is only in counties such as Yingde, Chenghai, Lianxian, Huaxian, and Gaoming. Guangxi's land is not suitable for planting opium, so there are also few opium seedlings. The situation of the abolition of opium prohibition is almost the same as in Guangdong. (5) Yunnan, Guizhou, and Sichuan, famous opium producing areas: Yunnan, Guizhou, and Sichuan are special areas for opium production in China. Farmers who plant opium in the three provinces do not sell all of it. A small number are kept for their own use because opium smoking has become a habit, and the demand is the same as for rice and wheat. The collection of opium tax is mostly handled by local garrison troops, and the county governments add additional subsidy donations, so there is a lot of resentment. As for the surplus opium, it is transported to Hankou in large quantities and distributed to various provinces in the country, so opium from Sichuan and Yunnan floods the market. Transportation in Guizhou is even more inconvenient. According to the survey, the reason for planting opium in the province is actually because transportation is lighter and adjusts the economy of the whole province. Because Guizhou's grain production depends on foreign demand, if there are no agricultural by-products to offset it, the economy will collapse. Transportation is difficult, and opium is easier to export, so many people are happy to plant it. The government has tacitly approved it for the sake of the province's finances. (6) Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, and Shanxi, where eradication is almost complete: Opium seedlings revived in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces in the 16th year of the Republic of China. Most of the opium seedlings in Jiangsu Province were in the counties north of the Yangtze River, and in Zhejiang Province, they were mostly in the areas east of Zhejiang. In the 17th year, the Zhejiang Provincial Government strictly implemented opium prohibition and eradicated opium seedlings vigorously. People did not dare to break the law, and all those who had them were eradicated. There were occasional discoveries in remote lakes and mountains where transportation was inconvenient, but they were purely for the sake of poor rural people, and the Zhejiang Provincial Government had no tax collection. In the 19th year, the Chinese National Anti-Opium Association investigated the opium planting situation in Zhejiang. The result was that there was no opium seedling found in the 18 counties south of the Yangtze River and the 2 counties north of the Yangtze River in Jiangsu Province, and in the 13 counties in eastern and western Zhejiang Province in Zhejiang Province. As for Shanxi, it had been cleared up early in the years. The survey in the 17th year found some in Zuoyun and Yangqu counties. Jiangxi originally belonged to the opium transportation area, and very little opium was planted. The survey in the 17th year also found it only in Longnan and Yudu counties. In general, the scourge of trafficking and smoking narcotic drugs in the four provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Jiangxi, and Shanxi is not less than in other provinces. If the opium seedlings are planted, they are more strictly prohibited than in other provinces. Even if they are found, they are rare. It can be concluded that. (7) Guandong, which is adjacent to bad neighbors: Liaoning and Heilongjiang provinces have always planted very little opium. The Jilin authorities have never advocated opium planting and any opium tax, so there is no trace of it. According to recent surveys, the situation in Liaoning and Heilongjiang provinces is slightly better than before, but opium seedlings are mostly found in areas with convenient transportation and lively areas. It is not known why this is the case. In the area bordering Russia in China, Russians have repeatedly violated the border and planted opium without authorization, which has repeatedly caused disputes. The Jilin opium planting survey only found a little in the forests of Fangzheng and Dunhua counties. (The following is omitted due to the loss of the original manuscript)

The Situation in Shanghai: The recent efforts of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau to prohibit opium are due to two reasons: (1) Shanghai is the largest commercial port connecting China and foreign countries and is the hub for the transportation of drugs from the north and south provinces. (2) The concessions in Shanghai are often the escape routes for all those who commit crimes. The jurisdiction of the law and the police have not been recovered, and it is difficult to completely eliminate these situations. This situation is very complicated. The efforts of this bureau to prohibit drugs are three points: (1) Investigate and seize transportation agencies (2) Investigate and prohibit sales and smoking agencies (3) Investigate and prohibit the sowing of opium seedlings. There is no sowing of opium seedlings in Shanghai, so most of the opium cases investigated by this bureau are transportation and sales. The following is a report on the opium cases investigated and seized for transportation and sales in the full year of the 19th year and from January to March of the 20th year: In the 19th year, there were a total of 082 opium cases and a total of 1,795 opium criminals. From January to March of the 20th year, there were a total of 497 opium cases and a total of 720 opium criminals. All the above cases were transferred to the Shanghai Local Court for prosecution according to law after they were investigated and seized along with the physical evidence. Compared with the 1,678 opium prohibition cases and 2,406 opium criminals in the 18th year, it has been reduced by 24%. If this ratio is maintained, it can be completely eliminated within five years, but the concessions are an exception, so there is no considerable certainty.

The Style of the Leader of the Japanese People's Party

South China Shipping Resumes 102

Guangdong Releases Detained Ships

Chinese Ships Prepare to Resume Services

Yu Shun Released: The South China Shipping Line's "Yu Shun" ship, previously detained by the Guangdong authorities, has been approved for release, according to a telegram received yesterday by the bureau from the Guangzhou branch. The ship is expected to leave for Shanghai via Xiamen on June 2nd. However, the ship's machinery and boiler need to be repaired and cleaned before it can sail. Therefore, the China Merchants Bureau intends to have it repaired at the No. 8 Dock immediately after its arrival in Shanghai tomorrow. It will only be able to resume operations after the repairs are completed. The ship has been detained in Guangdong for a total of one month.

Cargo to Shantou and Xiamen: Ships to Xiamen from Shantou first unload cargo in Shantou. From mid-May, Chinese ships completely stopped going to Xiamen. The laying of mines began after May 20th, following the same procedure as in Shantou, with pilot launches only allowed to operate during the day. At night, the port is closed. As a result, Chinese ships have uniformly avoided both locations. A large quantity of miscellaneous grains purchased in Niuzhuang, Andong, Shanghai, and other places, whose shipment has been delayed, is now planned to be transported. Merchants from both regions first requested Shanghai-based Chinese shipping companies to charter British ships like the "Zhejiang" to transport the cargo from outside the ports of Shantou and Xiamen, to avoid detention. Yesterday, with the release of ships like the "Yu Shun" from Guangdong, merchants in Shantou and Xiamen changed their minds. They telegraphed the Guangdong authorities, requesting that Chinese ships be allowed to freely travel to Xiamen and Shantou without being detained, and that the restrictions on entry and exit times be followed. It is expected that Chinese ships can be dispatched directly upon their return, without the need to hire foreign ships as substitutes. It is reported that this matter is likely to be resolved, and South China shipping routes will soon be open.

Yesterday's Silk Factories Shut Down 103

Three Major Reasons for Shutdown

Waiting for Public Bonds to Resume Operations

This municipality's silk factories have suffered greatly due to the sharp decline in raw silk sales to foreign firms last year, resulting in extremely low silk prices and high raw silk costs, leading to significant financial losses. Before last Lunar New Year's Eve, factories reduced shifts and stopped machinery due to lack of funds. This spring, silk merchants borrowed money from financial institutions against dry cocoon warehouse receipts to purchase cocoons and start production in order to maintain workers' livelihoods. At one point, over fifty factories resumed operations in Shanghai. However, the European and American silk markets became increasingly sluggish. Grade B silk was priced at only seven hundred and fifty to six hundred taels per bale, causing factories to lose three to four hundred taels per bale. Furthermore, the spring cocoon harvests in Jiangsu and Zhejiang were exceptionally poor. Consequently, the attitude of various manufacturers became increasingly negative, and more than twenty have announced shutdowns. As of yesterday (June 2nd), all one hundred and six silk factories in Shanghai have ceased operations, leaving tens of thousands of workers unemployed. The reasons for the shutdown are threefold: (1) Workers are demanding the restoration of previous wage levels starting June 1st. Given the current low silk prices and high raw silk costs, factory owners are already struggling to maintain the current situation and cannot bear additional burdens. (2) The spring cocoon harvests in Jiangsu and Zhejiang this year were exceptionally poor, with only thirty percent of the normal yield. The quality of the cocoons is poor, and the price is high, making it increasingly difficult to sustain silk production. (3) Financial conditions are extremely tight. Silk industry public bonds have not yet been issued, and silk factory leases are expiring. (Shanghai silk factory leases typically expire on June 1st each year.) Although six out of ten silk factories in Shanghai have renewed their leases, merchants are finding it difficult to raise capital and resume operations. Due to these three factors, all silk factories in Shanghai uniformly shut down yesterday. The resumption of work in various factories depends on the issuance of silk industry public bonds, after which about forty factories are expected to resume operations. Whether the remaining factories will resume operations depends on a bountiful summer cocoon harvest, sufficient raw material supply, and a global surge in silk prices.

Achievements of the Eurasia Aviation Corporation 104

Arrived in Manchuria Much Earlier Than Expected

Fixed Aircraft Routes Between Shanghai and Manchuria

The Eurasia Aviation Corporation's Shanghai-Manchuria flight operations began at the end of last month. A reporter from the Japanese "Daily News" visited the company's secretary, Sun Mutang, yesterday, who provided information on the route conditions and flight plans, as follows:

Triumphant News: The company received telegrams each time the plane reached a station. Four telegrams were received: (1) Nanjing, May 31st: "Eurasia 4 (aircraft number) flew north at 7:30." (2) Jinan, same day: "Eurasia 4 arrived at 10:30, departed at 10:50." (3) Peiping, same day: "Eurasia 4 arrived in Peiping at 3:15, switched to aircraft number 2, departed at 4:30 for Linxi." (4) Manzhouli, June 1st: "Eurasia arrived in Manzhouli at 10:20 due to favorable winds, circled once, landed safely. Eagerly viewed by various sectors." According to the company's schedule, the flight was supposed to arrive in Manzhouli at 12:00 noon on June 1st. However, it arrived as early as 10:20, one hour and forty minutes ahead of schedule, which was truly unexpected.

Fixed Aircraft Routes: The company uses aircraft numbers 1 and 2 for the Peiping-Manchuria line, because the route from Shanghai to Peiping is shorter and more stable, while the route from Peiping to Manzhouli is longer and has colder weather. Aircraft numbers 3 and 4 are used for the Shanghai-Peiping line. The engines of aircraft 1 and 2 are more powerful than those of aircraft 3 and 4. Aircraft 1 and 2 will be used to continue from Peiping to Manzhouli instead of Aircraft 3 and 4, and the same is also applicable to the transition from Manzhouli to Shanghai.

Returning to Shanghai Today: Aircraft number 4, which arrived in Peiping on May 31st, was replaced by aircraft number 3, which flew to Manzhouli. Aircraft number 2 departed from Manzhouli at 9:00 AM yesterday and returned to Peiping. Aircraft number 4 will then fly back to Shanghai early this morning, arriving at the Shanghai station at 1:30 PM. It is also reported that wireless telephone installations are underway at all locations, and the telephone at the Shanghai station will be completed within days.

Grand Parade to Prevent Cholera 108

Starting at 1:00 PM on June 6th

Participation of Chinese and Foreign Boy Scouts

June 6th is the date for the citywide grand parade to prevent cholera, with the participation of Chinese and foreign Boy Scouts. Initiated by the Capital National Health Administration, the parade is jointly organized by the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, the Public Health Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement, the Health Bureau of the French Concession Municipal Council, the Harbor Quarantine Station, the Shanghai Boy Scouts Council, and the Shanghai British Boy Scout Association. The preparations are largely complete. The following is a summary of the latest news:

Participation of Boy Scouts from Various Schools: The participation of Boy Scouts from various schools in the grand parade to prevent cholera is being coordinated by Wang Gang, the General Commander of the Chinese and Foreign Boy Scouts, and the authorities of the various schools. The Chinese side will have more than 1,000 participants, and the British Boy Scouts will have more than 200. All Chinese and foreign participants will wear their uniforms and be assigned to different teams. Participating Boy Scout groups from various schools include: Patriotic Girls' School, Guangzhao Public School, Chinese Women's Physical Education School, Municipal Business Association, Jinan University, Southeast Women's Physical Education School, Fudan Middle School, Guanghua University, East Asia Physical Education College, China Physical Education College, Liangjiang Women's Physical Education School, Chengzhong Middle School, Guangzhao Charity School, Moore Memorial Church School, Pudong Middle School, Shanghai Middle School, Yucai Middle School, and others. Propaganda Printing: The Municipal Health Bureau, the Public Health Department of the International Settlement, and the French Concession Health Bureau have jointly printed 20,000 large posters and slogans for display on the walls of thoroughfares in the Chinese-administered areas on June 4th and 5th. The posters and slogans are written in simple Chinese, French, and English, so that passersby can understand and be warned. The illustrations are also clear and informative, showing how flies, unclean food, spittoons, and night soil buckets can transmit cholera. 300,000 leaflets have been printed for the Boy Scouts to distribute along the parade routes to the public. The slogans on the leaflets are: "Do not eat fruits contaminated by flies or filth! Do not eat raw, cold, or unboiled foods! Do not eat millet! Do not eat liangfen or arrowhead cakes! Do not eat ice cream made with unhygienic ice! Do not use natural ice! Prevent flies from coming into contact with your food! Do not overeat; eat in moderation!"

Fifty-Two Squads: The purpose of this parade is to raise awareness among the public about cholera prevention. The scope of the work is also wider than in previous years. The various models, flags, and slogans prepared for the parade are divided into fifty-two squads. In addition to over fifty police officers maintaining order along the route, the Boy Scouts will carry models made of paper and wood, representing filthy water, sickbeds, coffins, and clean water. Each squad will have a megaphone to shout slogans along the way.

Shanghai Office of the Trademark Bureau to Be Closed 109

Office to Cease Operations from the 15th of This Month

The Shanghai office of the Trademark Bureau of the Ministry of Industry was established in Shanghai during the 16th year of the Republic (1927). It has provided significant convenience to local stores in handling trademark matters. Recently, the Ministry of Industry, in order to reduce expenses, has decided to close the Shanghai office, effective the 15th of this month. From then on, trademark matters will be handled directly by the Trademark Bureau of the Ministry of Industry in Nanjing. The Shanghai office has already notified the various accounting firms and commercial organizations accordingly.

Zhou Zuomin Discusses the Prosperity of Peiping's Municipal Administration 112

Talks Before Leaving Shanghai

Zhou Zuomin, General Manager of Jin Cheng Bank, came south for the opening of his bank's Nanjing branch. He was then selected as a representative of Peiping to the National Assembly and attended the National Assembly. Now, he is traveling to Qingdao for the opening of his Qingdao branch. A reporter from the Continental Press went to interview him before his departure from Shanghai to inquire about the current situation. Mr. Zhou said that he is dedicated to the banking industry and his purpose is solely to develop China's commerce and finance. He has no opinions on politics and finance, as they are not within his scope. However, regarding the prosperity of Peiping, as he is also a special member of the committee, he believes that the future development of the former capital holds great promise. In the past six months alone, the population of Peiping has increased by more than 20,000 households. This is because Peiping is the most suitable place for residence, with a comfortable lifestyle, fair prices, pleasant climate, and developed education, which attracts people from all over who seek a comfortable life. In terms of education, Peiping University, Tsinghua University, and Yanjing University are all renowned institutions of higher learning, and leaders in the domestic education sector are striving to make Peiping an education center, concentrating renowned scholars and students from all over the country. Peiping occupies an extremely important position in the history of our country, with many historical sites that are valued by archaeologists and historians. Therefore, one can broaden one's knowledge in Peiping. Knowing the past allows one to predict the future. Another often-overlooked factor is that Peiping is the intersection point of our country's major railways, the terminus of the Han-Ping, Sui-Ping, and Liao-Ning railways. With the planned addition of warehouses along the various routes, Peiping can also become an important commercial center. Nearby is our country's best Longyan iron ore mine, in which an investment of 5 million US dollars has already been made in machinery alone. Those involved are actively progressing forward. To revitalize the market in Peiping, we should start by promoting local Peiping products, such as the globally renowned carpets and other famous handicrafts. If concerned individuals can work together, Peiping will not be difficult to leap into the ranks of our country's metropolitan cities.

Yangtze River Pilot Training Institute Awards Graduation Certificates Yesterday 113

Ministry of Navy Issues Instructions

The Yangtze River Pilot Training Institute, established by the Ministry of the Navy, held a certificate awarding ceremony at 2:00 PM yesterday at its location on Municipal Government Road, for the second examination in the Songhu area. The representatives from the Ministry of the Navy, including Wu Guangzong, Director of the Hydrographic Office, and representatives from various naval agencies, and over ten people attended. After the customary rituals, the Director of the Institute, She Zhenxing, delivered the opening remarks.

Remarks by the Director: This institute has held two certificate awarding ceremonies. The first class consisted of 249 qualified candidates, held last month. Today is the second, with a total of 79 candidates. Except for one student who needs to make up studies due to poor performance, the rest are all excellent. I am deeply gratified. Our country's pilotage rights have fallen into foreign hands, posing a great crisis to national defense. Therefore, the Ministry of the Navy is willing to spend huge sums annually to establish this institute, which bears a great mission, and you gentlemen have a great responsibility. I hope you will strive to win honor for the country.

Instructions from the Ministry of the Navy: The pilotage industry is of great importance to maritime power, military affairs, and commerce. Only nationals should be allowed to serve as pilots, which is a common practice in all countries. Since our country opened trade with various countries, our seaports and inland rivers have actually allowed foreigners to engage in this business, which is a case of the guest usurping the role of the host. It is painful to speak of the drawbacks. The Yangtze River basin is the heart of our country, where merchants gather and ships ply. If the leadership of navigation is taken away by foreigners for a long time, the loss of sovereignty will be the greatest. Moreover, the dangerous areas along the river are related to military secrets. If foreigners are allowed to spy at will, the danger will be even greater in the event of war. The Ministry of the Navy, in light of this, has specially established this institute to provide training, starting with the Yangtze River and gradually extending to other areas, in order to restore complete sovereignty. The pilots in the Songhu area are well aware of the above points. The Ministry has specifically appointed Wu Guangzong, Director of the Hydrographic Office, to deliver instructions at this examination and awarding ceremony. I would like to briefly state the purpose of establishing this institute and the responsibilities of the hydrographic personnel, hoping that everyone will bravely move forward and strive to actively recover the previously lost pilotage rights and take responsibility for them ourselves. This is what all patriotic compatriots should do under the rule of the party. The Ministry has high hopes.

Speech by the Director of the Hydrographic Office: This institute has not been established for long, and hundreds of people have already qualified in the examinations. The Director of the Institute has spent a lot of effort in promoting and guiding. The faculty is excellent, and you have been well-trained. The results of the examinations are excellent, which is commendable. The government is actively working to recover pilotage rights, and the need for pilotage talent is even more urgent. After completing your studies, you should strive to improve, seize this opportunity, work together, and quickly catch up to completely take over the pilotage rights. You have a glorious career, which is also what I hope for. After the speech, Director She presented certificates to the officers in order.

The Xin Case Support Association Announces Its Dissolution 115

Following the serious injury inflicted on Mr. Xin Haishan, an employee of the Changhe Bank in this city, by a French patrolman's bullet on April 7th, a committee to support the Xin Haishan case was formed by various sectors to negotiate. Now that the French authorities have acknowledged our demands and the negotiations have concluded, the association announces its dissolution effective today. Yesterday, the association sent a special letter to the French Consul, urging him to report the resolution of the case to our government, and also prepared a document to report the details of the resolution to the Municipal Government for record. Excerpts of the original text are as follows: (1) Letter to the French Consul: "Regarding the case of the French patrolman No. 158 in your concession shooting Xin Haishan without cause on April 7th, the country was indignant. Since the incident, there has been no adequate relief measure, which has left a deep and negative impression on our friendly nations. Fortunately, after negotiations between Mr. Du Yuesheng, the Chinese taxpayer in the French Concession, and your consulate, it was agreed that in addition to bearing all medical and miscellaneous expenses for Mr. Xin's injuries, compensation for losses would be provided, a formal letter of apology would be issued, and the perpetrator would be suspended. The association has no objection to this plan. However, as this case has been formally negotiated by the government, we request that your consulate promptly inform our government of the above measures for the purpose of closure. We also hope that you will be deeply vigilant to prevent similar unfortunate incidents from happening again, so as to maintain the friendship between our nations and preserve the dignity of your country." (Omitted) (2) Document submitted to the Municipal Government: "Regarding the case of Mr. Xin Haishan, an employee of the Changhe Bank in this city, being seriously injured by a bullet fired by a French patrolman No. 158 of the French police on Yong'an Street on April 7th, the associated groups have submitted the circumstances and sent representatives to request serious negotiations. Now, after negotiations between Mr. Du Yuesheng of the Chinese Taxpayers Association of the French Concession and the French Consul, the French authorities have agreed to bear all medical expenses for Mr. Xin's injuries, compensate for losses of one thousand yuan, and promise to apologize and punish the perpetrator. For the sake of peace, the associated groups have reluctantly agreed to end the matter. As the task has been completed, we announce the dissolution of the association effective today. In addition to informing the French Consul to promptly inform our government of the above resolution measures, we are submitting a document detailing the resolution to your government for record. This is for the public benefit." (3) Letter to the various groups: "Since the unfortunate occurrence of this case, we have been deeply grateful for the righteous indignation and support of all sectors. Now, after negotiations between Mr. Du Yuesheng and the representatives of the association and the French Consul, an agreement has been reached on compensation, apology, and punishment. The negotiations have come to an end. However, one hand is hard to clap, and a single tree cannot make a forest. If it were not for the solidarity of all sectors and the continuous support, it is unknown when this case would have been resolved. We are sending this letter to express our sincere thanks. Compensation and apology are only temporary measures of appeasement. Only by completely recovering the concessions can we eliminate the problems permanently. We urge our compatriots to rise up and strive for it."

Strike by Binding Workers Yesterday 116

The third strike by binding workers has been ongoing for five days. It continued yesterday. The following is a report of the situation from the Daily News and the New Voice News Agency:

Dispatching Enforcers: Yesterday morning, the union dispatched enforcement teams. Lu A'gen and Chen Qingfa were appointed as team leaders for the eastern district, Pu Jin Yuan and Feng Shaoquan for the southern district, Lu A'xiang and Lu Jianqiu for the western district, and Xue Lanxin, Shen Changjiang, Xia Songfu, Li Baolin, and Chen Zhitin for the northern district. Team members were selected from the members in various locations and were sent out to enforce order, advising workers not to take any extreme actions to prevent reactionary elements from taking the opportunity to cause chaos.

Dismissal of Workers: Ma Hongji Binding Works on Zhizhi Garden Road suddenly dismissed three workers, including Zhou Xuechuan, yesterday. Zhou and others immediately reported this to the union. The reason for the dismissal is unknown. The workers will negotiate with Ma Hongji today. Mediation Today: The labor and management sides have not yet been in contact, and their attitudes are still quite distant. No one from the Social Bureau went to mediate. It is reported that mediation will begin today.

Workers' Declaration: Yesterday, the workers issued a declaration outlining their hardships, stating that the highest wage for workers is only seventeen or eighteen yuan, and as low as five or six yuan. There has been no increase in five years. After repeated appeals, the management initially agreed to a 10% raise, but how can this meager amount suffice? They pledge to increase wages by 40%. They have no choice but to strike to awaken the management when they give no sincere reply.

Binding Works Destroyed: Xinhua Yi Xin Records on East Huade Road, Shen Quan Ji on Rehe Road, Wang Quan Ji on Xiangshan Road, Xiehe Lujin Ji, and Lu Zhen Ji are still operating as usual yesterday. The striking workers found that these were breaking the strike discipline, so they went to question them. Arguments arose during the dialogue. The books in the above works that have not been completed have been vandalized. At Xinhua Yi Xin Records, there was also assault and injury to fellow workers. The guild has presented this to the party and government agencies for investigation and to uphold the hardship of businesses. According to guild sources, the striking workers each carried a bundle of incense and some even held long ingots when going to various works. It is not known what the purpose is.

Petition of 1,500 People
