The Dachan Shipwreck to Be Arbitrated Immediately and Salvaged 119

Obstructs Waterway, Forced to Be Salvaged

Arbitration Will Not Allow Further Delay

After the Dachan and Dahua ships collided outside of Wusong on April 14th, the Dachan ship sank. The losses of the ship have been verified by the Dahua Company, including 85,000 taels for the ship's hull, 11,000 taels for new repairs, 30,000 taels for one year of ship rental, 1,713 taels for ship equipment, 610 taels for ship crew wages, 50 yuan compensation for each of the 43 staff, totaling 1,581 and a half taels, 1,813 taels for the pensions of five deceased individuals, 1,620 taels for paid insurance fees, 12,000 taels for cargo losses, and 3,200 taels in losses at the Zhongxing Ship Rental Office, totaling over 140,000 taels. Because the arbitration has not yet been completed, the captain, first and second mates, engineers, and other crew members are still being paid monthly.

Arbitration in Progress: The responsibility for the sinking of the Dachan ship is said to be due to the error of the Dahua ship of Pingan Company, but Pingan is not responsible. The two sides have decided to request arbitration to determine the truth. Dahua has repeatedly urged, but Pingan has repeatedly delayed. Now, because the customs is urging a quick resolution to remove the sunken ship, Dahua has asked the shipping guild to urge Pingan Company to fulfill the arbitration. The arbitrators have been appointed by both sides, and the Shipping Association has scheduled a meeting next week to set the date for arbitration. According to the owner of Dahua, as soon as it is discussed next week, a verdict must be made and there must be no further delays.

Customs Salvage: Because the Dachan is sinking in a navigation channel, in accordance with Article 26 of the Maritime Law, the customs can salvage or blow it up. The customs has decided to salvage the sunken ship and has contacted the Tokyo Salvage Company. The salvage fee is 77,000 yen per day, equivalent to about 180,000 Shanghai dollars. A contract has been signed, and one-third has been paid in advance by the customs. The customs has also notified the Dahua Company that salvage will begin immediately, and the towing fee should be borne by the party responsible for the accident. Evidence of Negotiations: The Dahua Company cannot object to the salvage, but is worried that there will be nothing to base the arbitration on once the ship is salvaged and has sent a letter to customs requesting that the salvage be delayed. Customs rejected this request and replied Dahua saying that Japanese salvage technicians had been instructed to draw a picture of the ship as it sunk to prove the ship's position and damage, which will not affect the arbitration. Therefore, they will go to salvage the ship immediately.

Fish Tax and Fishing Industry Tax Waived, Yet Dada Still Collects Fish Tax Inspection Fees 120

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Orders Full Refund

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has issued a letter stating that since the National Government clearly announced the exemption of fish tax and fishing industry tax, Dada Company's ships are still collecting fish tax inspection fees as before, which is a violation of the law. Therefore, the chamber specifically sent a letter to the company yesterday, ordering it to immediately stop collecting the fish tax inspection fees that have already been collected and refund them in full. Furthermore, the letter inquired as to which agency the company is collecting these taxes on behalf of, and requested that the company refuse to collect on behalf of any agency in accordance with the National Government's clear order. It also requested that the company investigate the agency that is privately entrusting the company to collect the taxes in violation of the order, so that a report can be submitted to the National Government for review.

Minutes of the Meeting of the Nanbang Rice Merchants' Association 121

The Nanbang Rice Merchants' Association convened a meeting of all members from various inland ports the day before yesterday at the Cuixiu Hall in the Yimiao Temple for their annual meeting. Members attending included Jin Zhongpu, Yan Xiaoquan, Zhu Zixiang, Chen Qinsheng, Huang Shengyuan, Yang Yongyuan, Xu Yinfu, Pang Bosen, etc. Yan Xiaoquan was elected as chairman, Wang Disheng as recorder, and the meeting began with the usual formalities. The chairman then reported on the association's income and expenditure for the 19th year, followed by Xu Songda reading letters and documents from various places. Subsequently, various matters were discussed: (1) The association received a letter from the Tongli Rice Industry Association requesting the rectification of measuring rice with standard measures and postponement of the deadline. The association then forwarded the letter to the Doumi Industry Association, urging them to earnestly rectify the situation. Now, a repeated letter has been received. After deliberation, it was decided to extend the deadline by one day, making a total of three days. The question of whether to approve the extension for measuring rice with standard measures was put to a vote, and it was decided to allow an extension of one day. If rice merchants fail to measure rice with standard measures after the deadline, the salesmen and fellow inland traders, whose interests are at stake, should report to the association for strict urging. Rice merchants must measure rice with standard measures without delay. If rice merchants procrastinate, the association will notify the trade to temporarily suspend transactions to encourage them to reflect and maintain their interests. (2) The association received a letter from the Doumi Industry South Market Office requesting that inland traders ensure that the rice shipped to Shanghai is of uniform quality, with the same quality from top to bottom, and urging that hot rice not be loaded onto boats to avoid losses to both parties. The association decided that this practice, which dates back several decades, should be rectified voluntarily by inland traders to achieve effective cooperation between the domestic and foreign rice industries. The Wujiang Rice Industry Association will notify its members not to seek gains through luck and cause losses. (3) If any of our fellow traders incur losses due to the rising cost of goods in recent years, and thus find it difficult to sustain their business, and therefore submit a letter requesting an increase in commissions to supplement their income, how should we consider increasing commissions? The association decided to allow a discretionary increase of one point in the original commission, effective from June 1st. Commissions for sales made before May 31st will be settled in accordance with the previous rules to ensure clarity.

Local News Two

Russian Kills Military Police 124

Li Guorui and Shen Lisheng both died

Sis Kotuo Quluo Arrested

The first battalion, first company, fourth platoon of the military police regiment stationed at the Suzhou Station of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway dispatched soldiers to a checkpoint at 7 p.m. the night before last, as usual, to patrol between Suzhou and Kunshan. At around 10 p.m., the first group of three soldiers, near the Weiting Station, noticed a suspicious figure pacing back and forth in front of them. The soldiers ordered the person to stop. However, it was late at night and the fog made it difficult to see clearly. Although the person stopped and raised both hands upon hearing the order, they were holding two loaded handguns in their hands, which were difficult to see from a distance. When the soldiers approached, they realized it was a Russian and were about to step forward to question him when the Russian pulled the trigger and fired four or five shots at the two soldiers in front. The two military police officers, Li Guoduan from Jiangxi and Shen Lisheng from Changzhou, were hit in vital areas and died on the spot. The military police officer behind them, upon hearing the gunfire in front, realized something had happened and stepped forward to pursue the suspect. However, the suspect had already fled. The officer immediately arranged for the two injured military police officers to be taken to Shanghai on a special night express train to Tongren Hospital for treatment. At the same time, he notified the garrisons at nearby stations to search for the suspect. At dawn yesterday morning, a Russian named Sis Kotuo Quluo was apprehended at Weiting in Kunshan and was considered a major suspect. He was immediately taken to the regimental headquarters for interrogation. The two injured soldiers died in the hospital yesterday afternoon due to their severe injuries.

Careless Handling of Chemical Products at China Merchants Wharf 125

Two Laborers Scalded

Yesterday morning (the 2nd), the China Merchants Wharf on Broadway had the Java Company's ship, Jema, unloading a large number of dangerous chemical products, such as sodium and caustic soda. At about 10:30 a.m., as the last item was being brought ashore, a box suddenly exploded, immediately spreading to the chemicals on the wharf. Flames soared and were impossible to approach. The warehouse and the ship were also affected. Although the crew and laborers poured water to extinguish the fire, it only made the fire worse. When the Fire Brigade arrived upon receiving the report, they used yellow sand, charcoal ash, and oil to extinguish the fire. It took fifteen minutes to extinguish the fire. During the firefighting, two laborers were scalded. One suffered severe burns on the head, arms, and body, while the other suffered minor burns. The scalded laborers were identified as Huang Yi, 34 years old, and Qu Jinwei, 23 years old, both from Jiangbei. They were sent to Tongren Hospital by the Hongkou Fire Brigade for treatment.

Li Guojun's Daughter Sues for Divorce from Her Husband 126

Her Heartfelt Complaint is Moving

The Court Will Convene a Hearing Soon

Li Guojun, the granddaughter of the late Grand Secretary Li Hongzhang, has a daughter, Jia Zheng, who married Zhang Jin, the son of a Qing Dynasty General Zhang. Li and Zhang were originally old relatives, as Li Hongzhang's sister also married into the Zhang family, and Jia Zheng's aunt also married into the Zhang family. Because of the two generations of old relatives, Jia Wei was betrothed to Zhang Jin when she was five years old by her parents. They married in Shanghai on the 26th day of the eleventh lunar month in the 17th year of the Republic of China. At that time, the Zhang family's business was declining, and Jin Jiang was addicted to opium. Jia Zheng expressed her dissatisfaction, so her parents persuaded her and promised to give her a dowry of 20,000 yuan, with 8,000 yuan used to buy clothes and jewelry, and 12,000 yuan deposited in the bank to collect monthly interest to cover living expenses. After the marriage, Zhang Jin Jiang lived with his wife's family at No. 710 Xianyi Lane, New Chongqing Road. Last year, his father-in-law, Li Guojun, passed away, and Jin Jiang planned to take his wife back to their ancestral home in Hefei to take care of family affairs. The departure was scheduled for January 19th of this year, but Li expressed her dissatisfaction and left home on January 16th. At the same time, she was suffering from illness and was hospitalized. However, as a weak woman with no ability to earn a living, she found it difficult to make ends meet. Therefore, she filed a petition with the Special District Court, requesting that her stepmother, Jia Zheng, who was born out of wedlock, be given the 12,000 yuan deposited in her name by her father. The court held a hearing on the matter, but the case remained unresolved because both sides held different views. After Zhang Jin Jiang learned of his wife's whereabouts, he also filed a petition with the court, requesting an order for them to live together. A hearing was held in the mediation chamber on May 27th. The defendant, Li Jia Zheng, was unable to attend due to illness and was represented by lawyer Ge Zhaoji, who stated that the defendant had left home on January 17th because she could not bear the plaintiff's abuse. Furthermore, the plaintiff had used obscene language to insult the defendant on the second night of their marriage (the plaintiff had said that he had seen the defendant's face as a prostitute standing on the street in front of the Xian Shi Company's door). The defendant was mentally devastated by this insult and requested a divorce. The judge examined the statements and ruled that mediation was not possible. Therefore, Li Jia Zheng, through lawyer Ge Zhaoji, again submitted a petition to the Special District Court yesterday, requesting a divorce. The petition was written in parallel prose style, written by Jia Zheng herself and revised by the lawyer. The petition stated that the defendant had many bad habits and did not provide for her support. Because mediation failed, she was suing for divorce. The petition stated: "I, a daughter of the famous Li clan, was betrothed to the Zhang family in my youth. Obeying my parents' orders and relying on the matchmaker's words, I looked forward to growing old together for a hundred years and had been married for three years. I have continued my studies, understand etiquette, treat my husband as an elder, and attend to family affairs diligently. I hoped to sing and follow in harmony, to compose good poems, and to have a harmonious family. How could I know that my husband, Zhang Jin Jiang, is of base character and perverse disposition, regarding money as dirt and addicted to gambling like life itself. He calls out at the gambling table and uses the opium den as his bedroom, indulging without awakening, neglecting his duty to provide for me. I have tried to dissuade him with kind words, but he resents my loyal advice. I rise early and sleep late, only to suppress my anger. My husband squanders his wealth, using my dowry to seek pleasure. He indulges in gambling and opium, but when his money is exhausted, he is unable to satisfy his desires. His reputation diminishes, and he becomes angry and resentful. His words are violent, like a mad dog. He comes and goes freely, like a wild horse that has escaped its reins. Even over the smallest matters, he becomes angry and violent, abusing me to the point of whipping me. Alas, even if I do not die of hunger and cold, I will die from the beatings. I am not a blade of grass or a tree, who has no heart. All who hear of this are saddened, and all who see this are grieved. Thinking of this, my heart is broken, and my mind is shattered. Because I have been humiliated too much and cannot bear to endure it any longer, I requested mediation for divorce on the fifteenth day of May. My husband did not appear and even fabricated false statements to sue me in court, concealing his own faults and blaming his wife for absconding. His heart is lost, and he has abandoned reason. There is no possibility of living together again. Although we are husband and wife in name, we are like enemies. Such an evil family is like being in hell. The laws of the country are strict and do not allow the abuse of wives. Justice is clear and should be sought from the authorities. I would rather freeze and starve to death than be beaten and humiliated. I beg you, Your Honor, with your clear judgment and iron face, to uphold justice and protect human rights. Therefore, I humbly submit this petition, requesting Your Honor to summon Zhang Jin Jiang to court and order a divorce, so as to uphold the laws of the country and respect women's rights. Your merit will be boundless, and your kindness will be deeply appreciated." It is said that the court has accepted the petition and will summon both parties to court for a hearing soon.

House Collapse on Zhongxing Road Causes Multiple Casualties 127

Four Seriously Injured, Two Minor Injuries

Boy Wang Sikai Crushed to Death

More than twenty south-facing bungalows on Zhongxing Road, east of the Dayang Bridge in Zhabei, were old and dilapidated. The landlord, Lu Quanfu, originally rented them to a Chen from Jiangbei to build houses. Now, the land has been sold to Hui Ji Xing Construction. Because Chen's lease has expired, all the dilapidated bungalows have been demolished one after another. However, the house at No. 1917, where Xie Mao Chen Kee Rice Store was located, was not relocated until yesterday. The store was temporarily opened opposite the Tanzhiwan Security Corps. It was planned that once the new building was completed at the original site, the store would be moved back. Unexpectedly, at about 2 p.m., before all the assets had been completely moved out, the Jiangbei children in the vicinity rushed in to pick up copper coins. With a crash, the house suddenly collapsed, and those inside were unable to escape in time and were either injured or crushed to death. A total of four people were seriously injured: Zhou Peishan, 53 years old, Wang Xiaoxianzi, 12 years old, Xiao Xiaobao, 12 years old (all male), and Han Cuilan, 16 years old (female).

The four people above were all rescued by the First Section Fire Brigade and sent to Pushan Hospital for treatment. However, those with more serious injuries may be in danger of losing their lives. Two people were slightly injured: Zhu Yinhua, 14 years old (female), and Chen Xiaolaohan, 11 years old (male). A boy named Wang Sikai, 12 years old, was crushed to death. The Fourth District Public Security Bureau has ordered Wang Shaoting, the land security officer of the Taiyang Temple police station, to report to the Shanghai Local Court today for an autopsy. It is said that the deceased child's father is named Wang Wenbin, 42 years old, and his mother is Ms. Xu. He has an eight-year-old sister and is from Yancheng, residing at No. 1933.

Russian Youth's Grand Endeavor 128

Walking Around the World

Plans to Return to Shanghai in Three Years

In recent years, adventurers traveling around the world passing through Shanghai have used cars, airplanes, sailboats, bicycles, walked, or rode horses, which is already common. Recently, two adventurous Russian youths among the foreign residents in Shanghai, inspired by the trend, have embarked on a grand endeavor to walk around the world. They departed at 5 a.m. on Tuesday morning, planning to return to Shanghai in three years. They are only carrying a unicycle with a car tire to facilitate pushing. The two, named Borovsky and Hiles Xing, are both strong athletes in the Russian community. Their planned route is to start from Shanghai and follow the railway line to the capital, cross the river to Tianjin, Beijing, and Shenyang, and then take the route through Korea to Japan and the Philippines. Then, they will return to the Asian continent, enter Europe via India, walk across the United States, and return to Shanghai, with the aim of strengthening their bodies and increasing their knowledge.

The Daily Night Bank Debt Case is Being Actively Handled by Accountants Wu Zheng and Pan Zhaobang

The movable property of Huang Chu Jiu began public exhibition yesterday at the headquarters of the Daily Night Bank. Tickets were sold and many people visited. The exhibition was divided into four sections: calligraphy and paintings, furniture, antiques, etc., which were dazzling and beautiful.

Liang Yu, Suspected of Robbing Morphine, Declared Not Guilty 130

Liang Chengyu, a detective from the Second Squad of the General Inspection Office of the General Inspectorate, was suspected in the case of the robbery of 50,000 yuan worth of morphine from the home of Li Liansheng at No. 439 Male Lane, Chongqing Road. He was arrested by the police and reported to the Special District Local Court. After repeated court hearings, as previously reported, yesterday afternoon was the date scheduled for the verdict. The police escorted Liang to the Second Criminal Court of the Special Court. Judge Ge Zhiqin ascended the bench and declared Liang Chengyu not guilty. The police lawyer, Wang Yaotang, requested that the defendant remain in custody during the appeal period. Liang's lawyers, Ye Fukan, Yuan Yang'an, and Peng Jie, requested bail. As a result, bail was not allowed, and he was temporarily returned to custody.

Chen Yadao and Others Appeal the Case of Selling Military Arms and Opium; Hearing Concluded 131

Chen Yadao, Tang Lunpu, Wang Liding, and others from Ningbo traveled between Shanghai and Hankou to sell military arms and opium. The police investigated and seized four Mauser pistols and 300 yuan in banknotes from Tang Lunpu. Wang Xiaopu, a suspect, was also taken into custody. The Special District Local Court sentenced Wang Xiaopu not guilty, Chen and Tang to eight months imprisonment, and Wang Liding to six months imprisonment. The military arms were confiscated, and the banknotes were returned. However, Chen and Tang were not satisfied and hired lawyer Shen Xingxia to appeal. Yesterday afternoon, Song Yuan, the presiding judge of the Criminal Division of the Higher Branch Court, along with judges Gao and Ye, held a hearing. The appellant Chen Yadao claimed that he had not privately sold handguns with Tang Lunpu, nor had he handed handguns to Wang Liding. As for the opium receipt seized from him, it was for a transaction between Hankou and Yichang and was not brought to Shanghai for sale. Tang Lunpu's statement was similar to Chen's. Wang Liding stated that the Mauser pistol seized from him was brought by Qiu Qiansheng, who had a feud with Chen Yadao and others, so he falsely implicated them after being arrested. The Western detective handling the case reported on the investigation process. Then, the debate began. First, Shen Xingxia, the lawyer representing the appellants, stated that the original trial's conviction of the appellants was based entirely on Wang Liding's statement obtained during the police investigation. However, the reliability and admissibility of the statement needed to be examined. The lawyer also presented two facts that blamed the Chinese and Western detectives handling the case for negligence. From this, he inferred that Wang Liding's statement might also be wrong. Finally, he requested that the judge carefully consider the various points mentioned in the statement. Gan Jingxian, the police lawyer, and the prosecutor then made their arguments. The presiding judge then declared the debate concluded and scheduled a public verdict. Chen Yadao and others were returned to police custody.

Hotel and Restaurant Industry Requests Repeal of Increased License Fees 132

The Taxpayers' Association Sent a Letter to the Public Works Department Yesterday

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Public Works Department yesterday, stating: "We have received a letter from the Shanghai Restaurant Industry Association, which quoted Public Notice No. 4081 of the Public Works Department published on the 3rd of this month regarding the license fees for hotels and restaurants. In accordance with the resolution passed at the recent annual meeting of taxpayers, the new fees will be implemented from July 1st, with the fees for the first, second, and third classes being 100, 150, and 100 taels per quarter, respectively. The Chinese-operated restaurants in the Public Concession have been paying food and wine taxes in accordance with the department's regulations, and the department has issued licenses. Now, the department's notice only mentions restaurants and does not specify whether Chinese restaurants are subject to the revised regulations. It also states that it is in accordance with the resolution passed at the annual meeting of taxpayers, but it is not known whether this annual meeting of taxpayers includes your association. Such ambiguous language is not enough to inform the public and facilitate compliance. Therefore, we have attached a copy of the department's notice for your review and declare that the Chinese-operated restaurants unanimously deny bearing this heavy tax and earnestly request your association to argue on our behalf and continue to follow the old regulations. Furthermore, it is not known whether the restaurants mentioned in the notice refer only to those operated by foreign merchants or include both Chinese and foreign businesses. It is also not known whether your association has made a resolution on the annual meeting of taxpayers. We hope you will provide a reply." While this was being processed, the Shanghai Lower Hotel Industry Association also sent a letter, stating: "Public Notice No. 4081 of the Public Works Department, published on page 19 of the second issue of the Public Works Department's Chinese Gazette, dated April 30th of this year, states: 'Notice is hereby given that the department has decided to revise the license fees for all hotels and restaurants to be collected from July 1, 1931. The approved fee schedule is as follows: hotels, per quarter, first class 300 to 500 taels, second class 200 to 300 taels, third class 100 to 200 taels,' etc. Although it does not explicitly state whether it applies to Chinese or Westerners, it undoubtedly applies to all hotels in the concession. The quarterly license fees paid by our industry in recent years to the Public Works Department have been at the rates of up to 200 taels for first class, up to 90 taels for second class, and up to 60 taels for third class. Such tax rates are already excessive and do not match our business income. The Public Works Department is not unaware of the declining state of the hotel industry in the concession, which is on the verge of collapse. Therefore, they should find ways to reduce the tax burden to allow hotel merchants to recover slightly. However, instead, they suddenly increase the fees by five or six times, which is disappointing. At the beginning of this cooperation between the concession authorities and the citizens, all reforms should be carried out with the consent of both Chinese and Western taxpayers. If this move has not been agreed to by your association or passed, our industry cannot bear it. Therefore, we earnestly request your association to send a letter to the Public Works Department immediately, requesting the repeal of the fee increase notice and continue to collect fees at the old rates. Thank you for your public service." In addition to replying that the new regulations for increasing license fees have not been approved by our association, we are sending a letter to your association, requesting that you quickly withdraw the changed measures and continue to follow the old regulations. (New Voice Press)

Pig Pre-Slaughter Inspection Fee 133

Situation After Cancellation of Contractor

The pig pre-slaughter inspection fee was previously handled by a contractor, who charged 10 cents per pig. Now, the city government has decided to take over the operation itself and collect the fee at the original rate, after notifying the public. From the first of this month, the Municipal Finance Bureau will issue fee certificates, and merchants can purchase certificates at any time. The Municipal Health Bureau will carry out the inspection based on the fee certificate held and then issue an inspection form. It is said that after the implementation yesterday, the north and south meat merchants have purchased more than 1,000 inspection fee certificates from various tax collection offices. The rumor that no certificates were purchased yesterday is not true.

Appeal of Stallholders at the Eight Immortals Bridge Market 135

Request to Reduce Taxes and Licenses

The stallholders at the Eight Immortals Bridge Market sent a letter to the French Municipal Council, stating: "We respectfully submit this letter because we have previously sent a letter requesting your council to reduce the stall fees at the Eight Immortals Bridge Market. Because the reasons are complex, we fear that the previous letter was not detailed enough, so we are submitting another letter to explain the situation. We believe that your council has spent so much money and effort building the grand Eight Immortals Bridge Market for the sole purpose of revitalizing the vegetable market and increasing tax revenue. The stallholders also regard this as their only hope. However, since the announcement of the stall fees at the Eight Immortals Bridge, most of the large buyers have gone elsewhere, believing that the stall fees are so high that the selling prices must be higher. Therefore, they have all agreed to avoid the Eight Immortals Bridge Market. This is the first reason why the stallholders are affected. After the above situation has formed, the stallholders, because sales are not widespread, dare not import large quantities of goods. The burden is already heavy, so they cannot help but raise prices slightly. How could they know that sales would become increasingly scarce and goods would become increasingly scarce? At that time, even if they want to cut prices to attract customers, they are unable to do so. This is the second reason why the stallholders are affected. Because the stallholders are affected by this, those who are eager to find another way to make a living are gradually withdrawing from the Eight Immortals Bridge Market because the fees elsewhere are cheaper and sales are better. The remaining stallholders in the market feel increasingly lifeless. This is the third reason why the stallholders are affected. In summary, the stallholders are in a difficult situation and have no way to save themselves. They are forced to implore your council to follow the new example of reducing fees at the Public Concession vegetable market and temporarily reduce the fees to maintain the stallholders' initial livelihood. As for whether the vegetable market can prosper after the fee reduction, it is still another question. Some people may use the method of restricting the average number of donated licenses to adjust. Although the intention is good, it is still difficult to predict whether there will be any disadvantages. Even if it can be hoped to be successful, it cannot be done in a short period of time. Therefore, in order to alleviate the current difficulties, the stallholders propose that your council resolutely reduce the stall fees at the Eight Immortals Bridge Market first. Once the stall fees are reduced, the number of stallholders will inevitably increase. The Eight Immortals Bridge Market is solidly built, and the stallholders know that it is a long-term foundation. They only stay away because the fees are too high. If the stall fees are reduced, the enthusiasm of stallholders to apply will be expected. Although the above is not a comprehensive plan, it is enough to maintain the local area. We still ask the inspector to weigh the importance of the matter and implement it in advance, hoping to revitalize the market and benefit the people. We cannot express our respect and wishes enough." The representatives of all stallholders at the Eight Immortals Bridge Market, Wei Chunquan, Yu Ade, Chen Yunqing, Zhu Asan, Zhang Shaofu, Jin Xueqi, Zhu Yuxing, Cai Zhongfang, Wu Guanda, Song Xiaomao, etc., respectfully submit this letter to Mr. Fan Erdi, Inspector of the French Municipal Council.

Wang Yuandao National Medicine Store Grand Opening Today 138

Mr. Wang Yongmei, a respected gentleman of Shanghai, recognizing the urgent need to promote and improve traditional Chinese medicine, invested a large sum to build a three-story Western-style building in the French Concession's South Chu Jia Bridge area to open the Wang Yuandao National Medicine Store. Preparations have taken over a year, and the interior decoration is quite luxurious. Mr. Gu Youyu, a prominent figure in the pharmaceutical industry with extensive knowledge of traditional Chinese medicine, has been hired as the store's manager. Consequently, the selection of raw materials is of the highest quality, especially the sliced medicinal herbs, pills, and powders, which are innovatively prepared using scientific methods. To ensure the quality of its products, the store has established a factory in Shanghai's western suburbs specifically for manufacturing. Additionally, a glue factory has been established on the banks of West Lake in Zhuzhou to prepare donkey-hide gelatin and other animal glues. Furthermore, seasonal fresh herbs are grown in the Longhua customs-free zone. The scale of this store's operations and the completeness of its facilities mark a new chapter in the history of the traditional Chinese medicine industry. It is reported that the store's official opening and business operations today are sure to be prosperous.

Results of the Jiande Savings Association Election Announced 139

The Jiande Savings Association has been established for over a decade. Its original purpose was to improve society by promoting frugality and guiding savings. It is fundamentally different from other commercial savings associations. However, due to the name's emphasis on "savings," it is easily misunderstood by the public. Therefore, the committee convened last month to revise the articles of association in accordance with the Civil Code and renamed it the China Jiande Association, effective July 1st. Before that date, all member benefits and savings will be handled in accordance with the old regulations to maintain credibility. Notices have been widely distributed. In accordance with the new regulations, an election was held for the first board of directors on May 31st, with public counting of ballots at the association. The following twenty-five individuals were elected as the first board of directors: Wang Xiaoquan, Wang Yiting, Yang Xianfen, Yuan Ludeng, Chen Bingqian, Zhong Ketuo, Wang Binyan, Guan Ji'an, Hu Huisheng, Chai Yousheng, Feng Yunchu, Lu Fengzhu, Tu Kaizheng, Xia Yinggeng, Chen Gengyu, Chen Zhaoqi, Chen Zhongying, Zhang Yanling, Wang Gongkuan, Tan Yongye, Liu Huogong, Feng Bingnan, Hang Shijun, He Wuliang, and Chen Fukang. It is reported that Lan Ting and Tao Gongchen, among others, are the five alternate directors. The process of electing officers is currently underway.

Zheng Manqing Returns from Eastern Travels 140

Mr. Zheng Manqing recently traveled to Japan to participate in the Sino-Japanese Exhibition of Ancient and Modern Calligraphy and Painting, as previously reported in this newspaper. While the exhibition featured many fine works collected by connoisseurs from both North and South China, there were also numerous contemporary pieces. The works from the South were generally considered superior to those from the North, while the Japanese works were relatively few. Empress Dowager Shōwa attended the exhibition and spent three hours viewing the pieces, expressing considerable appreciation. She selected four paintings for purchase, two from the North (one by Chen Baochen, Grand Tutor, and one by Zhou Yang'an) and two from the South (one by layman Zhang Honghui and one by Wu Zhongxiong). Furthermore, the Empress, princes, dukes, generals, and other dignitaries also visited the exhibition in succession. The Japanese government's emphasis on art is evident. They offered high praise for the works of the faculty and students of the Chinese Art Academy. Wang Yiting, Zhou Xiangyun, Wang Jiezhou, and others have already returned to China. It is reported that Manqing went to Osaka for a meeting and, eager to return to the academy, did not stay long. He returned to Shanghai yesterday aboard the Nagasaki Maru, where the entire faculty and student body lined the riverfront to welcome him, creating a grand scene. It is said that Manqing's travel diary from his Eastern journey will be published soon.

Grand Gathering of 138 Elders 141

Happy Day, Longevity is Not Difficult

One Must Understand the Four Secrets to Health

The Shanghai County Public Education Center, in order to promote traditional morals and clarify local customs, held its second Grand Gathering of Elders yesterday afternoon at one o'clock. Prior to the event, the center printed pamphlets, registration forms, and distributed them to the district chiefs of the county, asking them to invite elders on their behalf. Simultaneously, advertisements were posted and oral announcements were made. As a result, a total of one hundred and thirty-eight elders, both men and women, from various districts arrived, leaning on canes and sticks. It was a grand occasion, welcoming over three hundred members of the public, creating a lively and bustling atmosphere. The venue was set up at the entrance of the center, with four colorful arches inscribed with "Sharing Extended Lifespans." On either side, the national flags and party flags fluttered in the wind. Upon entering, one reached the venue, with the slogans "Respect the Elderly as You Would Your Own Parents" and "Promote Traditional Morality" prominently displayed on the four walls. Two rows of long tables arranged in an "I" shape were set up for the elders to sit at. The stage was equipped with wireless telephones, phonographs, string and bamboo musical instruments, and other entertainment devices, demonstrating great thoughtfulness. The meeting began at half past one in the afternoon, with the center staff and students from the village normal school performing traditional Chinese music to welcome the guests. After the opening ceremony and formalities, Director Jin delivered the opening address, followed by welcoming speeches from Superintendent Zhu and District Chief Wu. Then, elder Tang Jundao delivered a speech on the harms of opium, gambling, alcohol, and lust. Chen Lianchen spoke on the importance of family education. Shen Yuebo, not accustomed to public speaking, asked Director Jin to convey his health-preserving experiences on his behalf, mainly focusing on four key points: (1) eat less, (2) moderate desires, (3) wake up early, and (4) exercise more and worry less. He also offered practical instructions on local customs and the promotion of traditional Chinese morals. In addition to opening the wireless telephone for audience participation, special refreshments were prepared. The First District Public Office and the cooperative attached to the center purchased high-quality towels and distributed them to all the elders present, creating an atmosphere of compassion and warmth in the quiet and bright countryside. The elders were full of energy, and the cheers resounded until after five o'clock, when the event ended with great satisfaction. It is reported that the ages of the participants were mostly above fifty, with the oldest being ninety-four years old.

One Man Killed in "Eating Tea and Settling Disputes" 142

Qian Yutang, a Shaoxing native who sells pickled vegetables in Chongde Alley, West Coal Ash Road, in the southern part of the city, had two guests at his home the other day. Xu Amao, a neighbor who had a feud with Qian, came to Qian's door and cursed loudly, calling Qian a "turtle with open eyes" and saying that he took in male prostitutes for money. Qian found the words very offensive and argued with him. Since both parties had some rogue qualities, they agreed to "eat tea and settle disputes" at Ximen the next day (i.e., the afternoon of the 1st). At that time, each side gathered more than thirty people to reason with them. Someone intervened to mediate and ordered them to disperse and discuss it again to avoid causing trouble. As a result, a group of people could not cause trouble in the teahouse in the city, so they flocked to the front of Chang Le Teahouse in Wansheng Bridge outside Ximen and fought each other. Zhu Acai on Qian's side was beaten, seriously injured, and fell to the ground unconscious. The two sides, seeing that they had caused trouble, began to flee, but the Second District Police Station was close by. After receiving the news, it immediately ordered the chief police officer to arrive at the scene and arrest Xu Amao and eleven others injured by Xu: Yuan Aquan, Wang Yaoquan, Fu Afang, Shen Xinhe, Cao Dagui, Cao Dachun, Wang Amao, Yuan Ashi, Wang Guofan, and Zhao Axin. In addition, Qian and five others on Qian's side, Wang Ali, Xu Agou, Liu Xiaoshang, and Yuan Jinrong, were taken to the station along with the injured Zhu Acai. The others had fled. It was confirmed that Zhu Acai was seriously injured and was immediately sent to the Southeast Hospital of Nanyang Bridge for treatment. Unfortunately, the injury was so serious that he died at night. Yesterday, the Second District Police Station transferred the 16 people to the local court for detention and ordered Dong Jianqing, the 13th district bail, to report to the hospital for an autopsy. Prosecutor Zhao and others were commissioned to come to the scene and found that Zhu Acai died of injuries sustained during his lifetime, ordering the family to collect the body and wait for legal action.

Child Run Over and Killed by Car 143

Zhu Zishan, a 13-year-old boy from Jiangbei, who lived in a flat in Tan Jiaqiao, Zhabei, made a living selling fruit. Yesterday morning at around 10 a.m., he was carrying a basket into the city when he was suddenly struck by a sedan-style car driven by Tang Yongyan, a large construction merchant, at the intersection of Bazilu. The license plate was number 4583. The child was knocked to the ground, and his head was severely injured. The case was investigated by Chinese constables Nos. 2383, who recorded the car's license plate number. The injured child was sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment but died at 5:30 p.m.

Lost Boy 144

At around 8 p.m. the previous night, Guarding Policeman Xiao Yinpei found a boy, about ten years old, wearing a short shirt and trousers of printed foreign cloth and blue cloth shoes, with a flat-top haircut, wandering around the Huining Wharf in the southern part of the city. He was immediately taken back to the police station, where the station chief questioned him about his origins. However, the child's speech was not very clear, and it was impossible to know his name and address. He was ordered to prepare a document and send it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for placement.

Detective Society's Detective Suspected of Extortion 146

Previously, a Westerner established the Shanghai Detective and Security Association and set up branches in Qinghefang, widely advertising that its mission was to investigate cases on behalf of merchants and hire bodyguards, etc. Therefore, it hired a number of detectives. Later, due to internal disagreements, a lawsuit was once involved, which was reported in the newspaper. After the lawsuit was over, the association became silent, and everyone suspected that it had disappeared. However, only the Qinghefang branch disappeared, while the general office still exists, currently managed by Portuguese national Tarsha, who is responsible for everything. The detectives hired are of mixed quality. Many of them misunderstand the nature of the association as being equivalent to a public detective agency. Therefore, they also pose as detectives, swindling and oppressing, doing everything possible. Naive people do not understand the situation and dare not resist even if they are exploited. Xu Wenlian, a Tongzhou native currently residing at 41 Huishan Road, has been working as a detective for the association and specializes in fraud. The day before yesterday, at 3 p.m., he suddenly broke into the home of Yang Fuqing, a Taizhou native residing at 1514 East Jiaxing Road, accusing Yang of running a brothel privately and demanding 50 yuan. Yang and his wife, Xu, worked as servants at a certain Japanese residence and were familiar with Xu, so they refused to be intimidated. Xu actually took out the private handcuffs he was carrying and forcibly handcuffed Yang, claiming to take him to the police station. While walking along the road, he encountered Chinese constables No. 2771. Fearing exposure, Xu quickly removed the handcuffs. The constable had already seen it and inquired about the situation, arresting Xu and taking him to the Harbin Police Station for detention. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Special District Local Court. Judge Xiao Xiefen questioned the police station's lawyer, who charged Xu with extortion, fraud, and obstruction of freedom, and presented the handcuffs as evidence. Yang Fuqing and his wife first recounted the course of events. Then, the police station presented Tarsha's written statement, claiming that the defendant was indeed a hired employee of the company, but that everything was non-compliant. Xu Wenlian blamed it on being drunk and requested leniency through his lawyer, Fan Gang. Judge Xiao sentenced him to two months in prison and confiscated the handcuffs.

Publication of a Monumental Work on Poetics 150

"The Source of Poetics," is the lifelong masterpiece of Mr. Guzi Xia Songsheng. It thoroughly analyzes and elucidates the art of poetry, with unique insights into phonology and philology. It includes a discussion of the evolution of poetics throughout the dynasties, tracing back to the Zhou and Qin dynasties and down to the Qing dynasty, all presented with insightful commentary that reads like a family treasure. It is an indispensable book for those who study Chinese classics and aspire to write poetry. The complete work consists of three thick volumes, finely printed on high-quality paper, priced at six yuan, and sold by Jinzhang Store, 580 Wuma Road, in this city.

Trade Association News 155

Department Store Industry: The Department Store Trade Association, in order to oppose the Shanghai Municipal Government's regulations on business tax rates, sent a letter to the Tax Rules Research Institute, stating: "In the June 1st newspaper, it was reported that the Shanghai Municipal Business Tax Preparatory Office passed the 56th item of the city's business tax rate, reducing the tax rate for foreign goods to 0.2%, and the 59th item, reducing the tax rate for department stores to 0.3%. The imbalance and disparity are unfair. According to the June 2nd newspaper, the Hankou correspondent reported that the Ministry of Finance's Tax Letter No. 1946 opened to explain that the regulations on business tax should clearly define the scope of whether department stores in major commercial ports belong to the foreign goods industry. Based on the nature of department stores, they are actually an expanded business of Beijing-Guangzhou foreign goods. Therefore, business tax should be temporarily collected in accordance with the Beijing-Guangzhou foreign goods industry, etc. Therefore, the tax rate stipulated by the Shanghai Municipal Government is obviously contrary to the Ministry of Finance's interpretation. Such discriminatory treatment is unfair, and our association can hardly recognize it. We hereby send a letter to request that the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau quickly revise it for public convenience."

Northern Goods Industry: The Northern Goods Trade Association was officially established on June 2nd. A general meeting was held on the second floor of the industry's market on Zhonghua Road. Representatives from the city's Party Department, the Social Affairs Bureau, and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce attended the meeting to provide guidance and supervision. Eleven executive committee members, including Qiu Yangzhi and Ling Licheng, were elected and sworn in immediately.

Kidnappers of Longshan Apprehended in Shanghai 156

Shen Xinbai, a secret investigator stationed in Shanghai by the Central Party Headquarters, was familiar with a detective from the Ningbo Public Security Bureau. Last month, the detective came to Shanghai from Ningbo and entrusted Shen with secretly investigating the whereabouts of bandits, saying that Xian Sheng, the 13-year-old son of Chen Yunkun, a resident of Beilongshan Town, Ningbo, had been kidnapped by bandits. It was heard that Shen was hiding at sea and asked for a secret investigation. Shen then instructed his nephew, Shen Zhenguang, to pay attention at all times. On the 27th of last month, Zhenguang told his great-uncle that he had learned that he had met Wang Farong, a Shaoxing native, on the way, who was forced to go to the Tongshang Hotel and write a letter to Chen Yunkun in Longshan, informing him that the child was now in Shanghai and that he could quickly send someone with 50,000 yuan to Shanghai to redeem him. The contact point was the Waibaidu Bridge, otherwise he would be torn up. He knew that these people were the bandits in the case. Therefore, after writing the letter, he returned and reported to Shen Xinbai, who reported it to Lu Xiang, the captain of the Detective Team of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau. After investigating and confirming that the bandits and their accomplices were hiding in two locations, 1026 North Chengdu Road and 4 Rongyangli, Wuding Road, they began at 10 a.m. the day before yesterday to dispatch detectives to the New Gate Police Station and first went to North Chengdu Road to arrest five people, including Wang Farong, his mother Wang Shen, his wife Wang Zhang, his cousin Wang Huabin, and his brother-in-law Zhu Xiaoquan. Then they continued to Wuding Road and arrested Wang's concubine Wang Wu and Wang Jinshun. The whereabouts of the hostage were still unknown. Yesterday morning, the group of men and women were sent to the Special District Local Court. Judge Wu Tingqi conducted the trial. Shen Xinbai and his grandson came to the court to testify. After Lu Captain requested extradition for trial, Judge Wu questioned Wang Farong and others and ordered that the seven bandits, men and women, be handed over to Lu Captain to be taken to the Ningxian Local Court for trial in accordance with the law.

Book and Newspaper Introductions

News Policy 158

— Huang Huanruo

By Du Chaobin

News policy—this is a very fresh term, because no one in our country has ever discussed it. Among those in our country who are engaged in the news industry, few have researched journalism, and they are even more ignorant of the situation in international news circles. Therefore, the news policy, which is used by modern imperialists as a backing and vanguard tool in political diplomacy, is completely ignored. This is a very painful and dangerous thing.

Our country's repeated failures in the international arena over the years have all suffered from the news policies of the great powers. Because the current so-called news policy, as Mr. Huang Tianpeng said, has become a propaganda policy for international confrontation, which is then used by ambitious people as a tool of politics and a weapon of diplomacy. For example, the May 30th Massacre created by British imperialists in the fourteenth year of the Republic of China, the May 3rd Jinan Incident created by Japanese imperialists in the seventeenth year, and the countless traces of aggression left by imperialists. The truth of the matter is self-evident, but because of the toxins of imperialist news policies, the propaganda has turned black and white upside down, confusing the public, so that a fair judgment cannot be obtained and grievances cannot be redressed. The loss of our country without a news policy is so great. In order to adapt to the requirements of national survival, it is imperative for our country to build a sound news policy. As Mr. Huang Tianpeng said, with a news policy, we will have a voice to the outside world, and the toxins of foreigners' propaganda will have nowhere to work; with a news policy, the immature newspaper industry at home will have a correct path to follow and can gradually develop.

However, although the emergence of journalism education in our country has had more than ten years of history, the contributions of journalism scholars to the news industry are very small. Apart from Mr. Huang Tianpeng's amazing amount of writings, only Mr. Ge Gongzhen and Mr. Xu Baohuang have made some contributions. Besides these, there are no achievements that can be admired. The past ten years or so have been in such a state, lingering until recently, in the past two or three years, when there has been some vigorous atmosphere. Works on the experience of studying journalism have also appeared like stars in the summer night, wearing brilliant clothes, one by one. Now, the book (News Policy) by Mr. Du Chaobin that I want to introduce is one of the most dazzling.

The entire book is divided into six chapters. At the beginning of the book, there are prefaces by Mr. Xie Liuyi, Mr. Ge Gongzhen, and Mr. Huang Tianpeng, all of whom have satisfactory criticisms of the book. The first chapter is the introduction, the second chapter is the origin of news policy, the third chapter is the current situation of news policy, the fourth chapter is the development of news policy, the fifth chapter is news policy and China, and the sixth chapter is the conclusion. After reading it chapter by chapter, I feel that this book is indeed worth reading. The narration is clear, the arguments are correct, and finally, the nationalistic news policy that our country's news industry should adopt is particularly the immortal point of this book. I would like to introduce the main points and values ​​of the book to readers chapter by chapter. I think those who care about the news industry will also be happy to hear about it.

The first chapter, Introduction. In this chapter, he explains the meaning and importance of news policy in great detail. Furthermore, he summarizes the current international news policies into two major categories: one is the news policy of various countries towards foreign countries, and the other is their news policy towards domestic affairs. The most noteworthy thing is that he divides the foreign news policies of various countries into three major factions:

(1) The news policy of capitalism, which uses high pressure as a means and aggression as a purpose.

(2) The news policy of socialism, which uses any means to achieve aggression.

(3) The news policy of nationalism, which uses peaceful struggle as a means to achieve independence, freedom, and equality.

Because the author clearly understands that the purposes of the red and white imperialists are the same, which is to give aggression to small and weak nations and harm the freedom and survival of small and weak nations, and believes that it is the most unreasonable news policy, it is definitely not the policy that our country, which is founded on the Three Principles of the People, should adopt. Therefore, he affirmatively said (Our country is trapped in the core of the news policies of capitalism and socialism, and its dangerous situation is unbearable to imagine. Apart from carrying forward and developing our nationalistic news policy, there is indeed no way to resist the powerful). And he said even more sincerely (Although the doomsday of the news policy of capitalism is not far away, the current situation is still in the hands of this force... Since our country cannot be outside of (the international community), we must use the news policy of nationalism to resist this fierce weapon, and we must also examine its situation in detail and carefully observe its functions, and think of ways to eliminate it. This is really a prescription for the right disease). It can be seen in what a dangerous state the position of our Chinese nation is in. The military and economic forces of the imperialists have come one after another to oppress us, and the toxins of their news policies are even more harmful, causing the loss of faith and understanding in the international community, so that we often suffer losses. Therefore, a news policy that fairly propagates the truth is what our country should urgently need to establish. The news policy that should be established is the nationalistic news policy that Mr. Du pointed out to us.

To be a mouthpiece for one's own nation and a tool for all the weak nations in the world to resist.

The second chapter, The Origin of News Policy. This chapter is further divided into three sections: one is the formation of news policy, the second is the elements of news policy, and the third is the merits and demerits of news policy. The formation of news policy is due to the rise of capital imperialism and the rapid progress of propaganda tools in scientific evolution. Therefore, the author said, "The poisonous flames of capital imperialism are rampant, and the sin is undeniable, but as a result, culture is progressing day by day, and people's wisdom is opening up day by day. The newspaper, which is the social teacher, is also prospering along with it." As for the elements of news policy, the author wrote this way: "The elements of news policy can be broadly said to be words and language, but strictly speaking, they can also be analyzed into several items such as being biased, unfaithful, and untrue." The author believes that "subjective emotional records in news writing and supplementary descriptions containing functions in language" are elements of news policy, because news policy must have subjective or functional opinions added. Because it has subjectivity and function, it is inevitable that there will be "partiality and bias," "unfaithfulness and untruthfulness," "partisanship," "fabrication of news," "inciting discord," "suppressing reason," and "painting clouds and supporting the moon" and other phenomena. Therefore, examples are given of the news issued by various news agencies under the control of the great powers. To sum it up in one sentence, it is nothing more than "selfishness." As for the merits and demerits of news policy, the author only refers to the news policy of the imperialists. The so-called merit refers to the help that the imperialists have gained from the news aggression policy, "so that their acquired irrational rights can be preserved, and the terrible doomsday will be postponed... It can even cover up their atrocities of massacring small and weak nations, causing the anti-revolutionary upsurge like a raging fire to decline." This is meritorious to the imperialists themselves. The so-called crime refers to the imperialists' use of this insidious and vicious news policy to control the small and weak nations in the world, making them unable to extricate themselves and blinding the ears and eyes of the international community, so that the cries of the small and weak nations cannot gain the sympathy of people from various countries, but instead regard the imperialists' tyrannical oppression as an appropriate arrangement. This is what the author considers to be the crime of news policy. However, it does not mention the nationalistic news policy that helps the small and weak nations that are oppressed in the depths of misery, which is a shortcoming of this chapter.

The third chapter, The Current Situation of News Policy. This chapter is divided into two sections. The first section explains the effects of the implementation of news policies by countries such as Britain and France at the beginning of the European War, "making Germany deeply hated by the people of the world before it suffered military defeats, and had to shoulder the notorious name of the culprit." Therefore, after the end of the European War, the great powers further used the conspiracy of their imperialist news policies to oppress the small and weak nations as much as possible. In order to make it easier for readers to understand the current situation of the news policies of the great powers, there is a detailed description of the recent international situation. The second section describes the tragic situation of various imperialists' news policies conquering small and weak nations and the increasingly popular and serious resistance of the awakened small and weak nations. Therefore, the news policies of the great powers will no longer be able to use their tricks and will face the doom.

The fourth chapter, The Prospects of News Policy, starts from the collapse of the Red and White

Page 20

The collapse of the two imperialisms and the "trustification" of the news industry prove the defeat of the great powers' news aggression policies. Furthermore, from "the Soviet Russia of communist countries falsely advocates the name of a news revolution policy and secretly conspires to confuse communist ideas" and "the news revolution policy rashly marches forward with a single will regardless of the conditions of its peers and society," it proves the unsuitability of the socialist news revolution policy. Moreover, from "No matter what nation, if it wants to survive on today's earth, it must have a strong and unyielding national characteristic and spirit. Otherwise, without the plunder of imperialism, it will be eliminated by natural selection. Therefore, the awakened nations have seen through this point and are focusing on cultivating the national spirit, and as for the news industry, they also advocate that it must be able to represent their national spirit as the best," it shows that the rise of the news self-reliance policy of nationalism is necessary and inevitable. Furthermore, according to the ultimate goal of the Three Principles of the People, the Great Harmony world, it explains that the news industry is advancing towards the trend of "news equality policy."

The fifth chapter, News Policy and China, explains that the underdevelopment of our country's news industry is caused by "internal factors" and "external factors," which has led to a cluster of crises in the future of the country and is still spreading with redoubled efforts. Based on the past undefeated experience, the first step in developing our country's news industry is to eliminate or break through the shackles of the news policies of the great powers. The most important methods are "promoting journalism education," "organizing a national news agency," and "self-manufacturing of printing tools." The narrative is correct and clear. Here is a brief summary.

The sixth chapter, Conclusion, explains the two aspects of the news industry's longitude and latitude. Finally, because "Our country is a giant among the weak and small nations, and the 1.134 billion oppressed people in the world are eagerly awaiting our country's rescue," it is determined that the news policies of imperialism and socialism are not the news policies that our country should adopt. At present, we must take on the responsibility of promoting the news self-reliance policy of nationalism.

The value of this book can be glimpsed from the above introduction of each chapter. The narration is clear and the arguments are correct, giving readers a very clear concept. As for the concise and sophisticated writing, it is even more so. The most brilliant and most suitable point for the current needs of our country in the entire book is that it proves from theory and facts that our country's news industry should adopt the news self-reliance policy of nationalism. Those who are interested in engaging in the news industry and who care about the news industry should have a copy at hand, which will be able to give you a lot of benefits in your career and knowledge. The publisher of the book is the Journalism Society of Fudan University, and the general sales office is the Guanghua Bookstore on Fourth Road. All major bookstores in various provinces and cities across the country also have distributors.

How to Be a Journalist 159

— Pingren

By Tian Lu, published by the United Bookstore

Because I am immersed in the dream of being a journalist, I often feel a pang of sadness when I walk past the entrance of Wangping Street. Although I have heard people hate the life of scissors, glue, and paste, and feel that this wastes the youth of a journalist, those of us who have not been immersed in this life always feel this way. This kind of sadness knows that every career must have its skills. Apart from pacing past the house in Baishi and looking blankly, I have never eagerly desired anything, because I know that I lack such skills.

When I passed by the bookstore, I saw that Mr. Huang Tianpeng, who has the most works on journalism, had written another book, "How to Be a Journalist." It's not thick, and this made my dream suddenly come back. Journalist—what a term worth cherishing! So I bought a copy. It's a book divided into nine chapters. He explores and instructs how to do it from all aspects of a journalist.

"Journalists have only relied on three things—scissors, glue, and red pen—to struggle for thousands of years to have today's position. Now, a pen is worth three thousand Mauser guns!"

Such a description reminds people of the life of a journalist.

The author also describes the position of a journalist very thoroughly. He said,

"Journalists are in the position of a third party. The only duty is to truthfully report the occurrence of a fact, regardless of its nature and its relationship with themselves. All facts that are most noticed and wanted to be known by the most readers should be faithfully recorded and impartially criticized, and no intention is allowed to exist in it. Therefore, the position of a journalist is transcendent in the company, independent in spirit, and objective in record." In modern times, our country has not yet recognized the position of journalists. In many cities and towns, it can be said that they respect journalists but are actually afraid of journalists, and a small part of journalists abuse their power—this is really due to a lack of understanding of the responsibilities of journalists.

If journalists want to guide the public to the right track, they must naturally have considerable self-cultivation. What they need is a healthy body, a lively and polite demeanor, abundant knowledge, specialized knowledge, a calm mind, ardent emotions, keen eyesight, a strong memory, agile wrists, diligent habits, a newsworthy nose for association, beautiful writing, moral cultivation, and a dignified personality. These are indeed qualifications that journalists cannot ignore.

Among the responsibilities of a journalist, the author lists the indispensable conditions, and the most important condition is to personally experience the "news battlefield," to be familiar with the situation of society, and to have extensive connections so that interviewing is easy, as well as to "understand the correct facts and have newsworthy principles."

In this book, it is not just demanding that the journalist have considerable qualifications, bear considerable responsibilities, and receive considerable education. At the same time, it also pays attention to the treatment of journalists. The book imagines ten items for the independence of personality, the protection of the profession, the improvement of position, public welfare facilities, mutual assistance among colleagues, preferential treatment, legal provisions, publication rules, insurance preparation, and others. Finally, it says, "What I said above is a speech at a journalist association, so it seems to be based on the journalists themselves and seems to have an antagonistic meaning with the capitalists. Actually, it is not. If the journalists themselves have a perfect organization, there will be greater achievements in the business. If the capitalists can recognize this point, it will be a good opportunity for labor-capital cooperation, and I believe that the news industry will have greater progress."

In addition to the main text, there are appendices (1) "How to Be a Journalist Reader," which details why to read newspapers, how to read newspapers, and what are the benefits of reading newspapers, (2) "An Autobiography of a Journalist," which shows the author's entire career as a journalist to the world.

In short, this book guides young people who want to enter the news industry in the right way. At the same time, only those who have a background in journalism can write such a clear and essential book. This is the author's latest contribution.

Publishing News 160

Mr. Liang Shaowen of Fudan University has been studying social problems with concentration. Based on his knowledge and experience over the years, he has recently written a book entitled "A New Discussion on Family Problems," totaling more than 50,000 words. The book lists all the essentials of family problems. The first part of the book cites and criticizes academic theories, and the second part lists various problems in the family, mixing solemnity and humor. It can be said to be a new book on family problems. Those who are concerned about this issue should have a copy in hand in order to understand the modern family organization and guidelines. It is also heard that the book is sold by major bookstores in this city, such as World Civilization, Beixin, and Qixin. The first edition is about to be sold out. Those who want to buy it can buy it as soon as possible to avoid missing out.

The China National Road Construction Association declared that the Road and Municipal Series of books compiled and translated by the association contains more than one million words, divided into essays, laws and regulations, engineering plans, construction special records, statistics and other compilations, containing all kinds of Chinese and foreign ancient and modern road and municipal materials. It is scheduled to be published in early July. The actual price of each book is 4.20 silver dollars. Pre-orders at the end of this month will only cost 3.20 silver dollars. In the past month, provinces and cities have pre-ordered more than a thousand copies. The pre-order address is the Association Office at 608 Labor Father Road.

Guidelines for Book and Newspaper Introduction Manuscripts 161

(1) The text is limited to introducing the latest publications at home and abroad. In addition to literary works, all books on politics, economics, law, science, education, etc., are included in the introduction, but boring books and newspapers will not be introduced.

(2) Pictures are limited to the latest works of new domestic and foreign writers and illustrations related to the text.

(3) Texts such as textual research or research on ancient Chinese books will not be published.

(4) Chinese paintings and photographs are limited to those related to the text.

(5) The text should not exceed 3,000 words at most.

(6) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(7) Do not draw pictures with blue ink or use colored paper. Use white paper and black ink.

(8) Please indicate that the manuscript is for the book and newspaper introduction editor to receive.

(9) Whether the manuscript is published or not, it will not be returned. If you need to return it, please state it in advance and attach sufficient postage stamps.

(10) Remuneration: 3 yuan, 2 yuan, and 1 yuan per thousand words for text; pictures and photos are also the same. Special manuscripts will be remunerated separately.

Social News

Twenty Countries' Writers Meet in Paris 162

One hundred and fifty writers from twenty countries met in Paris on the 27th of last month to discuss the establishment of a world federation dedicated to protecting the interests of novelists and other writers. It is expected that the result of the meeting will be the establishment of a general office in Paris, where writers from all over the world can submit difficult matters for research and response, especially in cases of copyright infringement. It is heard that newspaper reporters can also join the association. The association plans to meet for three days, with participants speaking in various languages and the Paris Municipal Bureau providing interpreters so that they can understand each other. French President Doumergue plans to host a banquet for the representatives on Friday with cabinet members to express the French government's concern for art and literature in the new culture. That night, the Mayor of Paris will hold a grand banquet at the Paris City Hall to welcome the representatives.

World Trade Volume Decreases Sharply in April 163

Decreased by 35% compared to the previous year and by 23% compared to last year

According to investigations, with the progress of the world economic panic, world trade is increasingly shrinking. For example, the trade of the three countries, Britain, the United States, and Japan, in April of this year decreased by 30% to 50% in both imports and exports compared to the same period last year, and also decreased by 23.3% to 37% compared to the same period last year. Himalayan Mountaineering Team Sets Off 164

Scheduled to Arrive in Early June

Kolkata News: The commander of the mountaineering team, Mr. Smith of England, aims to create a world record for climbing to the summit of Kamet (25,431 feet). Recently, he telegraphed from Joshimath, the mountaineering preparation site, that the mountaineering preparations of the group have been completed. It is said that 55 porters have carried mountaineering supplies and set off for Phishtiabuk. In addition to the commander, Mr. Smith, another group of Europeans, accompanied by some officers and porters, took transportation vehicles to Badrinath, 70 miles north of Joshimath. The group is scheduled to arrive in Phishtiabuk in front of the eastern Kamet Glacier in early June. The advance team and the main team plan to meet in Badrinath and pass through places such as Lohasan, Karul, etc., cross the Koli Pass, which is 12,400 feet high and covered with snow all year round, to Niki, east of Kamet. This plateau area on the side of the towering Dhauli Ganga Valley is the last village on the mountaineering route. Captain Beale, a famous mountaineer and currently an officer of the Bengal Governor's bodyguard, also participated in the group and is responsible for the logistics of the team.

World's Largest X-Ray Machine 165

Speed is About 99% of the Speed of Light, Able to Increase the Body's Resistance to Fungi

New York News: The world's largest X-ray machine, known as the world's largest, will be installed in the New York Hospital. Previous X-ray machines were limited to 200,000 to 300,000 watts. This new machine has a power of 900,000 watts. The electricity emitted by it travels at a speed of 184,000 miles per second. Its speed has the greatest speed in the universe, about 99% of the speed of light. The bulbs used in this machine are two, each with a length of 12 feet and a diameter of 20 feet. The power of light can pass through a 3-millimeter copper plate and penetrate 4 inches of iron, and the X-ray photography is clear. When used on the human body, the temperature inside the human body rises to 107 degrees Fahrenheit. With this high temperature, fungi will be extinct. However, whether malignant fungi such as tuberculosis and cancer will all be extinct has not yet been determined. The University of X-ray Medicine is currently conducting careful research and experiments on this. In addition, the effect of this machine is to increase the number of white blood cells at this high temperature to create a substance that resists fungi in the body.

Soviet Russia Tries to Develop Trade in Manchuria 166

Implementing a Dumping Kerosene Plan, With Warehouses in Major Ports in North China

Shenyang News: The Soviet Russian National Commercial Department is trying to develop trade in the Far East and complete its five-year plan. It has recently established a branch in Shenyang to open up sales channels for Soviet Russian goods in North and South Manchuria. It has now begun to sell samples of goods such as fish, cigarette paper, foreign wine, wool, and kerosene. Regarding kerosene, a special company has recently been established to specialize in selling kerosene. The Soviet Union intends to implement its dumping policy for kerosene, so British and American kerosene companies are on guard and actively preparing to compete. The Soviet Russian Kerosene Company plans to install kerosene storage tanks in major ports such as Yingkou, Harbin, Tianjin, and Changchun. Its large-scale export plan can be seen from this.
